401 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Truesdell v. State


No. 58628


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


304 P.3d 396; 2013 Nev. LEXIS 23; 129 Nev. Adv. Rep. 20



April 4, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended September 19, 2013.
Rehearing denied by Truesdell v. State, 2013 Nev. LEXIS 49 (Nev., May 31, 2013)
Reconsideration denied by Truesdell v. State, 2013 Nev. LEXIS 72 (Nev., July 18, 2013)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Truesdell v. Nevada, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 8389 (U.S., Nov. 18, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of invasion of the home in violation of a temporary protection order. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Douglas W. Herndon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant of home invasion and violation of a temporary protective order (TPO). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the organization's procurement of the TPO on the victim's behalf, after speaking with her by telephone, violated the procedure set forth in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 33.020(5) and violated his due process rights. The supreme court noted that the validity of a TPO was not an element that the State had to prove for the crime of home invasion or for a sentence enhancement for the violation of a TPO. Until the order was dissolved or modified or expired by its terms, it had to be obeyed. As defendant did not challenge the TPO in the issuing court, the supreme court could not consider his arguments pertaining to the TPO's validity in the appeal. Sufficient evidence existed to convict defendant of a home invasion in violation of a TPO, Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 193.166(1)(a), 205.067(1), as he went to the apartment where the victim was living and forcibly entered it without permission. The home invasion statute was constitutional. Trespass was not a lesser included offense of home invasion. The State's remarks constituted harmless error and did not substantially affect the jury's verdict. Defendant was properly ordered to pay $500 to the Indigent Defense Fund.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

402 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Masto v. Gypsum Res., LLC


No. 59557


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


294 P.3d 404; 2013 Nev. LEXIS 3; 129 Nev. Adv. Rep. 4



January 31, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 11, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Certified question pursuant to NRAP 5 from the United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit.
Gypsum Res., LLC v. Cortez Masto, 671 F.3d 834, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 22047 (9th Cir. Nev., 2011)



DISPOSITION: Questions answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit certified a question pursuant to Nev. R. App. P. 5 regarding the constitutionality of Nevada Senate Bill No. 358 (S.B. 358), in which the legislature adopted amendments that prohibited Clark County from rezoning land in certain areas adjacent to Red Rock Canyon National Conservation Area, including land owned by respondent landowner.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that S.B. 358 was a local or special law that regulated county business and established a system of county government that was not uniform throughout the State, in violation of Neb. Const. art. 4, §§ 20, 21, and 25. The owner argued that S.B. 358 did not fall within any exception. The supreme court found that S.B. 358 was a local law for the purposes of § 20 as it operated over only one particular portion of Nevada. S.B. 358 did regulate county business by permanently divesting the county of its zoning power of the adjacent lands; thus, it violated § 20. S.B. 358 violated § 21 because it was a local law that fell within an enumerated category of § 20. S.B. 358 violated § 25 because it established a system of county government that was not uniform throughout the State. S.B. 358 did not pass the first part of the Conservation District test, as the regulation of county business was enumerated in § 20. There was no natural resource justification.


OUTCOME: The first three certified questions were answered in the affirmative and the last certified question in the negative.

 

403 of 673 DOCUMENTS


City of Las Vegas v. Cliff Shadows Prof'l Plaza, LLC


No. 55877


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


293 P.3d 860; 2013 Nev. LEXIS 2; 129 Nev. Adv. Rep. 2



January 31, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal and cross-appeal from district court orders in an eminent domain action. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Kathleen E. Delaney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city filed an eminent domain action in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), to acquire a strip of property from respondent landowner, and the landowner counterclaimed for inverse condemnation. The trial court entered partial summary judgment against the city and partly granted the landowner's request for attorney fees. The city and the landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city wanted to use the strip for a road project. The landowner's predecessor received the land pursuant to a federal land patent which subjected the land to a right-of-way for roadway and public utilities purposes. The supreme court held it was error for the trial court to hold the land patent did not grant the city an easement because (1) the federal patent's use of the terms "right-of-way" and "subject to" created an easement on the land for roadway and public utility purposes, and (2) the city was entitled to use the easement, despite not being specifically named, as the patent's language created a public easement, and any ambiguities had to be construed in favor of the government. The city's use of the easement for a road project was not a taking, under Nev. Const. art. I, § 8(6), because (1) the easement's use fit within its scope articulated in the federal land patent, stating it was subject to an easement for "roadway" and "public utilities" purposes, and (2) the patent did not state roadways could be created only if they directly benefited owners of property issued pursuant to the Small Tract Act, former 43 U.S.C.S. § 682a.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment finding the city had no easement on the subject land was reversed, and its award of attorney fees was vacated. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

404 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. State


No. 57481


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


291 P.3d 1284; 2013 Nev. LEXIS 1; 129 Nev. Adv. Rep. 1



January 17, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Rehearing granted by Woods v. State, 2013 Nev. LEXIS 18 (Nev., Mar. 22, 2013)
On rehearing at, Substituted opinion at Woods v. State, 2013 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 1833 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a bench trial, of sex offender failure to notify appropriate agencies of change of address. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Connie J. Steinheimer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a pretrial petition for writ of habeas corpus and/or motion to dismiss the indictment. The Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), denied the petition. Appellant was subsequently convicted of sex offender failure to notify agencies of a change of address, under Nev. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 179D.550. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was originally charged via criminal complaint with failure to notify agencies of a change in address. Appellant filed a motion to dismiss. The parties agreed to reset the preliminary hearing to the State could file an opposition, but the State did not, and the justice court granted the motion to dismiss. Later, the State obtained an indictment against appellant for the same offense. Appellant filed for habeas corpus relief and/or dismissal, claiming the State acted with conscious indifference when it failed to oppose the motion to dismiss. The trial court denied the petition, and appellant was convicted. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction. The trial court erred in finding that the State's failure to oppose the motion to dismiss the complaint did not amount to conscious indifference, given that (1) the State had been served with appellant's motion to dismiss and did not oppose it, (2) the State was on notice that its failure to oppose could be see as an admission that the motion had merit, (3) no explanation was offered for the failure to act, and (4) the prompt filing for reconsideration did not excuse the State's failure to timely respond to appellant's motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction.

Beazer Homes Holding Corp. v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court of Nev.


No. 57187


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 723; 291 P.3d 128; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 120; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 66



December 27, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at View of Black Mt. Homeowners Ass'n v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court, 2015 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 1296 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Original petition for a writ of mandamus or prohibition challenging a district court order determining that, under NRS 116.3102(1)(d), a homeowners' association could litigate, on behalf of its members, construction-defect claims with respect to its members' homes without meeting NRCP 23's class action prerequisites.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner developer petitioned for a writ of mandamus, claiming that respondent Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, acted arbitrarily and capriciously by refusing to undertake a class action analysis.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the developer lacked a plain, speedy, and adequate remedy at law. Its petition raised important issues of law and public policy concerning the ability of common-interest community associations to litigate claims on behalf of their members in a representative capacity. The supreme court found that the district court abused its discretion in granting real party in interest association's motion for declaratory relief without analyzing the Nev. R. Civ. P. 23 requirements. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 116.3102(1)(d) standing did not obviate the need to evaluate the Rule 23 requirements. Rule 23's requirements had to be examined upon request.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted in part and a writ of mandamus was issued instructing the district court to conduct a proper Nev. R. Civ. P. 23 analysis; the developer's petition was denied as it pertained to a writ of prohibition.

 

406 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. State


No. 53632, No. 55086


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 598; 291 P.3d 1274; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 110; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 55



December 6, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Garcia v. Nevada, 134 S. Ct. 385, 187 L. Ed. 2d 25, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 5269 (U.S., Oct. 7, 2013)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jackson v. Nevada, 134 S. Ct. 56, 187 L. Ed. 2d 25, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 5255 (U.S., Oct. 7, 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Jackson v. State, 2017 Nev. App. Unpub. LEXIS 257 (Nev. Ct. App., Apr. 19, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeals from district court judgments of conviction based on similar questions regarding double jeopardy and redundancy. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Valerie Adair, Judge (Docket No. 53632); Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Jerome Polaha, Judge (Docket No. 55086).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant of attempted murder, assault, battery, and other crimes based on his actions in a single incident with a single victim. A jury of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County, convicted another defendant, for acts in a street fight, of murdering one victim, and, as to two other victims, attempted murder and battery. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Nevada held that no violation of the Double Jeopardy Clause arose from the multiple punishments for convictions, arising from single incidents, of attempted murder, assault with deadly weapon, and battery with deadly weapons because each offense contained an element not contained in the other. The court disapproved of Salazar v. State, 119 Nev. 224, 70 P.3d 749 (2003); Skiba v. State, 114 Nev. 612, 959 P.2d 959 (1998); Albitre v. State, 103 Nev. 281, 284, 738 P.2d 1307, 1309 (1987); and their "redundancy" progeny, to the extent that they endorsed a fact-based "same conduct" test for determining the permissibility of cumulative punishment. Rather than a focus on the facts or evidence in a specific case, the proper focus is on legislative authorization, beginning with an analysis of the statutory text. If the Legislature has authorized--or interdicted--cumulative punishment, that legislative directive controls. Absent express legislative direction, the Blockburger test is employed. Blockburger licenses multiple punishment unless, analyzed in terms of their elements, one charged offense is the same or a lesser-included offense of the other.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction in both appeals.

408 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. Bennett-Haron


No. 59861


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 580; 287 P.3d 305; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 96; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 54



October 25, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeals from a final district court order in consolidated cases granting in part and denying in part declaratory relief and denying a complaint for an injunction challenging the constitutionality of a county ordinance. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Joanna Kishner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, rejected the majority of appellant Nevada Highway Patrol Officers' claims against respondents and upholding all but one of the Clark County code sections pertaining to inquest proceedings related to officer-involved deaths. The judgment also dissolved the temporary restraining order and denied injunctive relief. The officers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The officers argued that their due process rights under the Nevada Constitution would be violated if they were forced to participate in the coroner's inquest process under the procedures set forth in the Clark County, Nevada, Code of Ordinances for inquests involving officer-involved deaths. The supreme court noted that under caselaw, the inquest process constituted an investigatory, rather than an adjudicatory, proceeding. As a result, due process protections were not triggered by the inquest process. Because Clark County had an appointed coroner, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 259.050(4) did not apply, and thus, justices of the peace were not authorized to participate in Clark County inquest proceedings. Respondent Clark County Board of County Commissioners unconstitutionally impinged on the Legislature's constitutionally delegated authority, Nev. Const. art. 6, § 8, by providing for the participation of justices of the peace in Clark County's inquest proceedings related to officer-involved deaths. Clark County, Nev. Code of Ordinances § 2.12.010(1) violated the Constitution. The entire inquest scheme for officer-involved deaths necessarily had to be struck down.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

409 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Busefink v. State


No. 57579


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 525; 286 P.3d 599; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 93; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 49



October 4, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to an Alford 1 plea, of two counts of conspiracy to commit the crime of compensation for registration of voters. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Donald M. Mosley, Judge.


1 North Carolina v. Alford, 400 U.S. 25, 91 S. Ct. 160, 27 L. Ed. 2d 162 (1970) (permitting a plea of guilt even though the defendant still maintains her claim of innocence).


Ass'n of Cmty. Orgs. v. Dist. Ct., 2010 Nev. LEXIS 1871 (Nev., July 15, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant, pursuant to an Alford plea, of two counts of conspiracy to commit the crime of compensation for registration of voters. The district court suspended defendant's sentence, placed her on informal probation, and required her to complete 100 hours of community service. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the central issue was whether Nev. Rev. Stat. § 293.805's prohibition on the payment of individuals based upon the number of voters registered violated U.S. Const. amend. I. Because § 293.805 did not place a severe burden on First Amendment rights, the supreme court considered the validity of § 293.805 pursuant to a less exacting standard of review. Because the statute's restriction on per-application and per-party payment of canvassers was narrow and an organization still had the ability to hire and pay voter registration canvassers, the statute did not result in a significant injury to First Amendment rights. Nevada had an important regulatory interest in preventing voter-registration fraud. The State's interest was sufficiently weight to justify § 293.805's limitation on the payment of canvassers. The term "register" as used in the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The term "based upon" in § 293.805 was not vague. A person who violated the statute would know that they were violating the statute. The intent would apply to the payment of workers based upon the number of voters registered.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

410 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Sheriff, Pershing County v. Andrews


No. 58713


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 544; 286 P.3d 262; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 94; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 51



October 4, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order granting a pretrial petition for a writ of habeas corpus and dismissing a charge for possession of an item commonly used to escape. Sixth Judicial District Court, Pershing County; Richard Wagner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sheriff sought review of an order entered by the Sixth Judicial District Court, Pershing County (Nevada), which granted respondent's pretrial petition for a writ of habeas corpus and dismissed a charge for possession of an item commonly used to escape under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 212.093(1).


OVERVIEW: Respondent was in custody in a county jail when officers discovered a cell phone in a box hidden underneath his bed. Respondent was charged with possessing an item commonly used for the purpose of escaping from custody. A pretrial petition for a writ of habeas corpus was filed to dismiss the charge on the grounds that § 212.093(1) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad and that its terms did not prohibit the possession of cell phones. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court did not consider the constitutionality of the statute as the plain language supported the dismissal of the charge. The items specified in the statute were those that could either be used to forcibly manipulate the confines of a jail cell, like a picklock or wire cutters, or to physically exit from a jail cell, like ropes or ladders. The omission of cell phones appeared to be deliberate as Nev. Rev. Stat. § 212.165(3) specifically prohibited inmates in state prisons from having cell phones without lawful authorization; this prohibition did not apply to county jail inmates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order.

 

411 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Winn v. Sunrise Hosp. & Med. Ctr.


No. 54251


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 246; 277 P.3d 458; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 61; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 23



May 31, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court summary judgment in a medical malpractice action. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Doug Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father, as guardian for his daughter, appealed a summary judgment for respondents, a hospital and the doctors, entered by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), in a medical malpractice suit.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that the accrual date for Nev. Rev. Stat. § 41A.097(2)'s one-year discovery period ordinarily presented a fact issue for the jury. When the evidence irrefutably showed that a plaintiff was put on inquiry notice, the trial court could determine the discovery date as a matter of law. The father was on inquiry notice, but not when he was informed that his daughter was brain dead as the trial court held. Rather, the father was put on inquiry notice when he was provided with a complete set of the hospital's records. Factual issues remained as to whether the hospital concealed records from the father so as to warrant tolling § 41A.097(2)'s discovery period. The father was to be given a chance to show that the hospital intentionally withheld records that would have hindered a reasonably diligent plaintiff from procuring an expert affidavit. The summary judgment was affirmed as to the doctors since the hospital's alleged concealment could not serve as a basis for tolling § 41A.097(2)'s statutory limitation periods as to the doctors, who played no role in the concealment. The claims against the doctors were time-barred.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment for the hospital was vacated, and the case was remanded so that the father could be afforded an opportunity to show that the hospital intentionally withheld records that would have hindered a reasonably diligent plaintiff from procuring an expert affidavit. The summary judgment for the doctors was affirmed.


 

412 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Schettler v. RalRon Capital Corp.


No. 56508


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 209; 275 P.3d 933; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 55; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 20



May 3, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 12, 2012.
Decision reached on appeal by Schettler v. RalRon Capital Corp., 2016 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 203 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court summary judgment in a contract action. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Elissa F. Cadish, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, granted summary judgment in favor of respondent lender on its breach of contract and personal guaranty claims against appellant debtor. The district court found that the debtor's defenses and counterclaims were barred by the Financial Institutions Reform, Recovery, and Enforcement Act of 1989 (FIRREA), 12 U.S.C.S. § 1821. The debtor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The debtor argued that FIRREA did not apply because the proceedings below involved the lender rather than the FDIC and because the FDIC failed to mail him notice of the specified bar date for filing his claims against the bank. The supreme court found that with respect to claims relating to acts or omissions of the failed bank, a successor in interest was entitled to benefit from FIRREA's jurisdictional bar. FIRREA's jurisdictional bar did not apply to defenses or affirmative defenses. Based on his allegations, the debtor may be able to demonstrate that he was entitled to recoup against any amount awarded the lender on its claims, up to the amount awarded. Because the debtor's affirmative defense raised unresolved questions of material fact, and because affirmative defenses were not barred by FIRREA, the district court erred in granting summary judgment in favor of the lender on its breach of contract and breach of personal guaranty claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

Maestas v. State


No. 48295, No. 54080


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 124; 275 P.3d 74; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 59; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 12



March 29, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 22, 2012.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Maestas v. Nev., 133 S. Ct. 275, 184 L. Ed. 2d 163, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6695 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Consolidated appeals from a judgment of conviction of first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon, attempted murder with the use of a deadly weapon, and burglary while in the possession of a deadly weapon and an order denying a motion for new trial in a death penalty case. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Donald M. Mosley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a death penalty case, appellant challenged a decision from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, which convicted him of first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon, attempted murder with the use of a deadly weapon, and burglary while in the possession of a deadly weapon. He also challenged a decision denying him a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant stabbed two children because he was seeking revenge after a drug deal went bad. One of the children died as a result of the injuries. Appellant was convicted and sentenced to death. He unsuccessfully sought a new trial, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the supreme court determined that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 175.556 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Next, a new trial was not warranted in this case. There was no proof of intrinsic misconduct by the jury foreperson, and the jury did not consider extraneous information. The foreperson also did not intentionally conceal any bias against appellant. An argument that the federal constitution required that aggravating circumstances and the balancing of aggravating and mitigating circumstances be alleged in the charging document was rejected. Challenges to the notice of intent to seek the death penalty were rejected. There was no error in admitting appellant's statement or a letter he wrote while incarcerated. Even though one comment made by a prosecutor was improper, it was harmless. Finally, a death sentence was properly imposed under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 177.055(2).


OUTCOME: The conviction and the order denying the motion for a new trial were both affirmed.

Wheble v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court


No. 58774


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 119; 272 P.3d 134; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 21; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 11



March 1, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended April 13, 2012.
Writ of mandamus denied, As moot Saxena v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court, 2012 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 410 (2012)
Writ denied by Wheble v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court, 2012 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 1081 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Original petition for writ of mandamus challenging district court orders denying petitioners' motions to dismiss and for summary judgment in a medical malpractice matter.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a physician and physician's assistant, filed a petition for writ of mandamus seeking relief from the decision of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, denying their motion to dismiss the medical malpractice action filed by plaintiffs, an individual and the estate administrator of the deceased patient, as untimely.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' medical malpractice claims were dismissed for failure to attach an expert affidavit as required by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 41A.071. Because the complaint never existed, the action was never commenced under Nev. R. Civ. P. 3. Thus, the district court was required to dismiss plaintiffs' second complaint reasserting the claims previously dismissed, because the statute of limitations had expired. The Supreme Court of Nevada held that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.500 did not save medical malpractice claims dismissed for failure to comply with Nev. Rev. Stat. § 41A.071; these claims were void.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted, and the court clerk was directed to issue a writ of mandamus directing the district court to dismiss plaintiffs' complaint.


 

415 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Pohlabel v. State


No. 55403


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


128 Nev. 1; 268 P.3d 1264; 2012 Nev. LEXIS 2; 85 A.L.R.6th 787; 128 Nev. Adv. Rep. 1



January 26, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended February 24, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a guilty plea, of felon in possession of a firearm. Fourth Judicial District Court, Elko County; Andrew J. Puccinelli, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Elko County, Nevada, that convicted him of being a felon in possession of a firearm in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 202.360, arguing that his conviction violated the right to keep and bear arms as secured by U.S. Const. amend. II and Nev. Const. art. 1, § 11(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that, despite his felon status, he had a constitutional right to possess a black powder rifle. On review, the court held that, while federal law currently permits felons to possess black powder rifles, that did not mandate that Nevada follow suit. The choice as to whether to deny felons the right to possess any and all firearms, as Nevada has done, or to permit them to possess antique firearms and black powder rifles, as Congress has done, was legislative, not judicial. Without a constitutional imperative demanding more exacting review, such distinctions did not invalidate state laws that differed from their federal counterpart. Further, the constitutional right of law-abiding, responsible citizens to keep and bear arms in the defense of hearth and home did not extend to felons. Because gun rights were among the rights of citizenship or the civil rights that a felon has historically been seen as losing by reason of conviction in Nevada, it was reasonable to read the reference to every citizen in Nev. Const. art. 1, § 11(1) to exclude unpardoned felons.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

416 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Nunnery v. State


No. 51870


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 749; 263 P.3d 235; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 87; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 69



October 27, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Nunnery v. State, 2011 Nev. LEXIS 121 (Nev., Dec. 20, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Nunnery v. Nevada, 132 S. Ct. 2774, 183 L. Ed. 2d 643, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 4654 (U.S., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon, two counts of attempted murder with the use of a deadly weapon, conspiracy to commit robbery, robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, two counts of attempted robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, and a sentence of death. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Sally L. Loehrer, Judge.
Nunnery v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court, 124 Nev. 477, 186 P.3d 886, 2008 Nev. LEXIS 52 (2008)
Brass v. State, 2010 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 59 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant of first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon, two counts of attempted murder with the use of a deadly weapon, conspiracy to commit robbery, robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, two counts of attempted robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, and a sentence of death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the notice of evidence in aggravation under Nev. Sup. Ct. R. 250(4)(f), the district court's decision to allow the late filing by the State was not arbitrary or capricious or exceeded the bounds of law or reason. Defendant failed to show that the testimony and documentary evidence of his prior drug conviction and social history were inadmissible, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 176.156(5). The weighing of aggravating and mitigating circumstances was not a fact-finding endeavor and the district court did not err in refusing to give the requested instruction. Defendant's requested instruction was properly rejected because it did not correctly state the weighing determination required by the Nevada statutes. Defendant failed to show that the late notice of evidence in aggravation prejudiced him in his defense of the great-risk-of-death aggravator. The evidence was sufficient for a rational juror to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant knowingly created a great risk of death to others as contemplated by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.033(3). The jury's verdict was supported by sufficient evidence. The death sentence was properly imposed and was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

417 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Ford v. State


No. 52272


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 608; 262 P.3d 1123; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 71; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 55



September 29, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 8, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of pandering of prostitution. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; J. Charles Thompson, Judge (sentencing; and David Barker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant of pandering of prostitution. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that to be convicted of pandering under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.300(1)(a), a defendant had to act with the specific intent of inducing his target to become or remain a prostitute. It rejected defendant's argument that the statute's omission of a stated intent requirement automatically meant that it provided for strict criminal liability. To read § 201.300(1)(a) as imposing strict liability would shift the crime's focus from the panderer's efforts to recruit prostitutes to the success of the recruiting program. The statute did not criminalize a substantial amount of protected expressive authority and thus fell to the First Amendment overbreadth doctrine. The statute did not prohibit abstract advocacy of prostitution; it forbade efforts to recruit a targeted person to work as a prostitute. The statute gave adequate notice of the conduct it prohibited and did not give law enforcement such standardless discretion that it authorized or encouraged seriously discriminatory enforcement. The crime of pandering did not require that the defendant's persuasion succeed. The failure to give a specific intent instruction affected defendant's substantial rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Hughes


No. 54327


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 626; 261 P.3d 1067; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 72; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 56



September 29, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 8, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order dismissing a charge of production of child pornography after concluding that NRS 200.710 is unconstitutionally vague. Fourth Judicial District Court, Elko County; Andrew J. Puccinelli, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Judicial District Court, Elko County, Nevada, granted defendant's motion to dismiss a child pornography charge. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court concluded that the term "minor" in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 200.710 was not unconstitutionally vague because it had a well-settled and ordinarily understood meaning: an individual under 18 years of age. Given the permanency of a visual depiction, it was rational for the Legislature to conclude that participation in pornography memorializing a sexual encounter required greater maturity from the participants than did the choice to engage in sexual relations. Under § 200.710 it was unlawful to use a person under 18 years of age in producing a pornographic performance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

City of Oakland v. Desert Outdoor Adver., Inc.


No. 53973


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 533; 267 P.3d 48; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 54; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 46



August 4, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 6, 2011.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Oakland v. Desert Outdoor Adver., Inc., 132 S. Ct. 1713, 182 L. Ed. 2d 252, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 1979 (U.S., Mar. 5, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order granting a motion for NRCP 60(b) relief from a domesticated foreign judgment. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Steven R. Kosach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the City of Oakland, California, attempted to enforce, in Nevada, a California civil judgment against respondent advertising company. The Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County, Nevada, granted the advertising company's motion to set aside the foreign judgment and quash execution of the judgment. The City of Oakland appealed.


OVERVIEW: The City of Oakland obtained a California civil judgment against an advertising company pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 5485(f) for erecting billboards in violation of Oakland zoning ordinances. Because Oakland was enforcing its individual rights under California's unfair competition laws to stop a private harm against the City, the assessment of statutory civil penalties was penal in nature; therefore, the Huntington penal exception to the Full Faith and Credit Clause applied. The California judgment did not fall under Nevada's Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 17.330-.400.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cortes v. State


No. 54747


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 505; 260 P.3d 184; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 46; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 44



July 21, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 6, 2011.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a conviction of possession of a controlled substance with intent to sell. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Linda Marie Bell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicting him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to sell.


OVERVIEW: During a routine traffic stop, the police developed a reasonable suspicion that the car's passenger, defendant, was armed and dangerous because he had a knife in his lap. A patdown search produced evidence of methamphetamine used to support his conviction for possession of a controlled substance. On appeal, the Supreme Court of Nevada upheld the district court's finding of reasonable suspicion because a reasonable officer could conclude that a frisk was necessary to protect himself and his partner. The officer's request for identification pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484A.730(1) did not constitute an illegal search or seizure, and defendant's rights under the Fourth Amendment were not violated when the officer placed his hands in cuffs to control the frisk. The Supreme Court of Nevada refused to interpret Nev. Const. art. I, § 18 more strictly than the Fourth Amendment. The district court did not abuse its discretion in evidentiary rulings or in settling the jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Berrum v. Otto


No. 54947


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 372; 255 P.3d 1269; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 37; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 30



July 7, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at North Lake Tahoe Fire Prot. Dist. v. Washoe County Bd. of County Comm'rs, 310 P.3d 583, 2013 Nev. LEXIS 80 (Oct. 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order granting a petition for a writ of mandamus in a tax action. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Brent T. Adams, Judge.
Vill. League to Save Incline Assets, Inc. v. State ex rel. Bd. of Equalization, 124 Nev. 1079, 194 P.3d 1254, 2008 Nev. LEXIS 97 (Oct. 30, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County, Nevada, issued a writ of mandamus requiring appellant Washoe County Treasurer to refund excess taxes paid by respondent taxpayers for the 2006-2007 tax year. The taxpayers paid the excess taxes because of a stay imposed in a pending appeal challenging a prior year's assessments. The Treasurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Treasurer argued that writ of mandamus was inappropriate because Nevada's statutory tax collection scheme provided the taxpayers with an appropriate legal remedy for overpayment of taxes and because he had no legal duty to refund the excess amounts. The supreme court found that the taxpayers were not denied relief but instead prevailed before the County Board of Equalization and, ultimately, the State Board of Equalization. They were not required to pursue the remedies in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 361.420 before seeking a refund under the procedural facts of the case. The State Board's failure to explicitly direct a refund did not abrogate the district court's power to enforce any other statutory duty to issue a refund. The remedies in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 361.405(4) were not applicable because the State Board did not need to direct the Treasurer to take action as a result of its decision. Under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 360.2935, the Treasurer had a duty to refund the excess taxes paid during the supreme court's stay of the County Board's equalization decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

422 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Nev. State Democratic Party v. Nev. Republican Party


No. 58404


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


256 P.3d 1; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 57



July 5, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Nev. State Democratic Party v. Nev. Republican Party, 2011 Nev. LEXIS 1759 (Nev., July 5, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District Court, Carson City, Nevada, granted a permanent injunction in a special election matter in favor of respondents, Republican Party and candidate, requiring that, for a person to be a "candidate of a major policy party" eligible for nomination under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 304.240(1), he or she had to have been designated as such, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 293.165. Appellants, Democratic Party and Nevada Secretary of State, appealed.


OVERVIEW: Respondents argued that Nev. Rev. Stat. 304.240(1) directed that the Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 293 general election laws applied except to the extent that Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 304 provided otherwise, and that 304.240 expressly provided the procedure for nomination and placement on the special election ballot of major party candidates through a process of self-nomination. The supreme court noted that the statute did not provide any plain method for major political party candidates' placement on the ballot. A major political party candidate was "designated" by the party central committee, not "nominated." Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 304.240(1) was ambiguous, as it was unclear the extent to which Chapter 293 was intended to apply to special elections. The Legislature enacted Nev. Rev. Stat. § 304.240 with the understanding that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 293.165 could be applied to a vacancy in office. Under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 304.240(1), the individual designated by the major political party's central committee, in compliance with Nev. Rev. Stat. § 293.165, may be placed on the ballot when he or she was nominated for special election by filing a declaration pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 293.204.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Aguilar-Raygoza v. State


No. 54667


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 349; 255 P.3d 262; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 29; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 27



June 2, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Aguilar-Raygoza v. Nevada, 132 S. Ct. 551, 181 L. Ed. 2d 397, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8037 (U.S., Nov. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of felony driving under the influence. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Connie J. Steinheimer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of felony driving under the influence (DUI), under Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 484C.110, 484C.400(1)(c). The Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County, Nevada, concluded he was ineligible for the alcohol treatment program because he had elected to go to trial rather than plead guilty or nolo contendere. The district court sentenced defendant to 30 months in prison and ordered him to pay a $2,000 fine. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: In a felony DUI case, the Supreme Court of Nevada considered whether it was unconstitutional to deny to defendants who exercised their right to a jury trial eligibility for the alcohol treatment diversion program set forth in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484C.340. The court held that the provisions of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484C.340 were constitutional. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484C.340 was not an unconstitutional burden on the exercise of the right to a jury trial under U.S. Const. amend. VI. The statute did not violate defendant's right to equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because it was rationally related to the legitimate governmental purpose of extending a proper degree of leniency in return for a guilty plea, which conserved scarce prosecutorial resources.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Clean Water Coalition v. M Resort, LLC


No. 57649


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 301; 255 P.3d 247; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 24; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 24



May 26, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 24, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal and cross-appeal from a district court summary judgment, certified as final under NRCP 54(b), declaring constitutional an Assembly Bill section that requires monies to be transferred from an entity created by agreement among local Clark County governments to the State's general fund for the State's unrestricted general use. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; David B. Barker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, granted summary judgment, in favor of respondent State, declaring constitutional an Assembly Bill section that required monies to be transferred from appellant entity created by an agreement among local Clark County governments to the State's general fund for the State's unrestricted general use. The entity and appellant businesses appealed.


OVERVIEW: The entity and business argued that because Assembly Bill (A.B.) 6, § 18 applied in only a single Nevada county, and only to users of the municipal or county sewer systems in that county, it was a local law, and because it applied specifically and directly to a single entity in the state to the exclusion of all other similarly situated, it was a special law. The supreme court found that the bill addressed statewide concerns through legislation that applied only to the entity and funds collected from wastewater-treatment users within a certain locality. It was special (pertaining only to the entity) and local (applying only to a particular locality). A.B. 6, § 18's mandate directing the entity to transfer money to the State's general fund for statewide-unrestricted-general use was an impermissible local and special tax, Nev. Const. art. 4, § 20. Since A.B. 6, § 18 was a local and special law that addressed a statewide concern to which a general law could have applied, it was not permissible under Nev. Const. art. 4, § 21. The district court erred by declaring it constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Landreth v. Malik

SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


127 Nev. 175; 251 P.3d 163; 2011 Nev. LEXIS 17; 127 Nev. Adv. Rep. 16



May 12, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 24, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for rehearing of Landreth v. Malik, 125 Nev. Adv. Op. No. 61, 221 P.3d 1265 (2009), an appeal from a district court default judgment. Eighth Judicial District Court, Family Court Division, Clark County; N. Anthony Del Vecchio, Judge.
Landreth v. Malik, 221 P.3d 1265, 2009 Nev. LEXIS 78 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Prior opinion withdrawn; reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a dispute between an unmarried couple concerning the ownership of real property, the state supreme court issued an opinion vacating the default judgment entered by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Family Court Division, Clark County, Nevada, for respondent boyfriend. He filed a petition for rehearing pursuant to Nev. R. App. P. 40. The state supreme court granted a rehearing.


OVERVIEW: This appeal involved an unmarried, childless couple who previously lived together and disputed the ownership of real property. Although Nev. Rev. Stat. § 3.223 did not give the family court division jurisdiction over such matters, the Nevada Legislature did not have the authority to limit the constitutional powers of a district court judge in the family court division. Therefore, the Supreme Court of Nevada held that the district court judge sitting in family court did not lack the power and authority to dispose of the case merely because it involved a subject matter outside the scope of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 3.223. The district court abused its discretion when it denied appellant girlfriend's motion to set aside the default without considering whether her boyfriend gave a proper notice of intent to take a default.


OUTCOME: The prior opinion was withdrawn; and the district court's judgment was reversed.

Berkson v. Lepome


No. 49261


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


126 Nev. 492; 245 P.3d 560; 2010 Nev. LEXIS 50; 126 Nev. Adv. Rep. 46



December 16, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 21, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order dismissing a probate and trust action and from a post-judgment order awarding attorney fees and costs. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Susan Johnson, Judge.
Lepome v. Berkson (In re Estate & Living Trust of Miller), 125 Nev. 550, 216 P.3d 239, 2009 Nev. LEXIS 65 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, awarded respondents' motion to dismiss appellants', decedent's nieces, claims of undue influence, breach of contract, fraud, elder abuse and neglect, intentional misstatement of facts, negligence, conspiracy and per se violation of Nevada law, and misconduct. The district court awarded respondents attorney fees and costs. The nieces appealed.


OVERVIEW: The nieces argued that the district court erred in dismissing their complaint because Nev. Rev. Stat. § 11.340 clearly and unambiguously granted them the right to file a new complaint after the supreme court reversed the jury verdict in their favor. The supreme court agreed with respondents' contention that § 11.340 violated the separation of powers doctrine, Nev. Const. art. 3, § 1(1), because it unconstitutionally interfered with the judiciary's authority to manage the litigation process and the supreme court's ability to provide finality through the resolution of a matter on appeal. The nieces' refiled complaint was subject to preclusion principles. Because the nieces' position was supported by § 11.340, it was an abuse of discretion for the district court to sanction the nieces for filing a frivolous claim. The attorney fees and costs awarded to respondents was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the motion to dismiss; the judgment was reversed as to the post-judgment attorney fees and costs awarded to respondents.

State v. Castaneda


No. 52911


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


126 Nev. 478; 245 P.3d 550; 2010 Nev. LEXIS 49; 71 A.L.R.6th 739; 126 Nev. Adv. Rep. 45



November 24, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 21, 2011.
Modified by, Rehearing denied by State v. Castaneda, 2010 Nev. LEXIS 62 (Nev., Dec. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order dismissing charges of indecent exposure after concluding that NRS 201.220 is unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; James M. Bixler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order entered by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which dismissed charges of indecent exposure against defendant on the basis that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.220 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with indecent exposure after § 201.220 after he was alleged to have intentionally and repeatedly exposed his genitals and buttocks while standing on a public sidewalk in front of a county jail. A witness in a nearby car observed defendant's conduct and contacted the police. On appeal, the court affirmed. While the statute did not define what it meant to expose one's "person" in an "open and indecent or obscene" manner, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.050(3) incorporated common law definitions. Based on such definitions, indecent exposure included the intentional exposure of one's genitals on a public street corner. However, § 201.220 could not be read so expansively as to permit conviction based on the exposure of one's buttocks alone. The court noted that the offense consisted of the intentional, open, and indecent or obscene exposure, not its visual observation by others.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded for further proceedings.

Candelaria v. Roger (In re Candelaria)


No. 55714


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


126 Nev. 408; 245 P.3d 518; 2010 Nev. LEXIS 43; 126 Nev. Adv. Rep. 40



October 14, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 21, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order granting a petition to remove a candidate for justice of the peace from placement on the ballot. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; James Bixler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of an order entered by the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which granted a petition by respondent county district attorney (DA) to remove the attorney as a candidate for justice of the peace from placement on the ballot.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was admitted to the state bar on October 17, 2006. In January 2010, the attorney filed her candidacy declaration. The DA challenged the attorney's eligibility pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 4.010(2)(a) as the attorney would not have been licensed to practice law for at least five years prior to the November election. On appeal, the court affirmed. The statutory language regarding eligibility under § 4.010(2)(a) was not ambiguous regarding the meaning of the term "years"; the language at issue anticipated that the attorney would be licensed and admitted for an exact period of time equal to not less than five years and provided a specified date by which the five-year period had to conclude - before the attorney's election or appointment to the position. Section 4.010(2)(a) did not violate the attorney's equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Nev. Const. art. 4, § 21 by creating different requirements for justices of the peace based on the population of the county and township in which the justice of the peace would serve because justices of the peace in highly populated areas would be likely to have busier dockets than those in more rural areas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Carrigan v. Comm'n on Ethics of Nev.


No. 51920


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


126 Nev. 277; 236 P.3d 616; 2010 Nev. LEXIS 30; 126 Nev. Adv. Rep. 28



July 29, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 14, 2010.
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by Nev. Comm'n on Ethics v. Carrigan, 562 U.S. 1127, 131 S. Ct. 857, 178 L. Ed. 2d 622, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 13 (U.S., 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by Nev. Comm'n on Ethics v. Carrigan, 564 U.S. 117, 131 S. Ct. 2343, 180 L. Ed. 2d 150, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 4379 (U.S., June 13, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order denying a petition for judicial review from a decision of the Nevada Commission on Ethics. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; William A. Maddox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being censured by respondent, the Nevada Commission on Ethics, appellant city council member petitioned for judicial review before the First Judicial District Court, Carson City, Nevada. The district court issued an order denying the petition, and the city council member appealed, arguing that his censure for alleged violations of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 281A.420(1)(c) violated the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that voting by public officers on public issues was protected speech under the First Amendment. Because Nev. Rev. Stat. § 281A.420(1)(c) directly involved the regulation of protected speech by a public officer in voting, it was subject to a strict scrutiny analysis. The court concluded that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 281A.420(8)(e) was unconstitutionally overbroad in violation of the First Amendment because it lacked necessary limitations to its regulations of protected speech. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 281A.420(1)(c) required officials to refrain from voting on matters in which they would be affected by their commitments in a private capacity to the interests of others, but because subsection (8)(e) provided an overly broad definition of what constituted a commitment in a private capacity, the abstention requirement for this category of relationships lacked necessary limitations to its protected speech regulation. Thus, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 281A.420(8)(e)'s application to a wide range of differing commitments and relationships was not narrowly tailored, was substantially overbroad, swept within its control a vast amount of protected speech, and violated the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court declared Nev. Rev. Stat. § 281A.420(8)(e) to be unconstitutionally overbroad in violation of the First Amendment and reversed the district court's order.

Polk v. State


No. 52733


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


233 P.3d 357; 2010 Nev. LEXIS 20; 126 Nev. Adv. Rep. 19



June 3, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 14, 2010. As Amended September 9, 2014.
Rehearing denied by Polk v. State, 2010 Nev. LEXIS 36 (Nev., June 3, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of second-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and discharging a firearm out of a motor vehicle. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Elizabeth Goff Gonzalez, Judge.
Polk v. Sandoval, 503 F.3d 903, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 21716 (9th Cir. Nev., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant of second-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and discharging a firearm out of a motor vehicle. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his constitutional right to confrontation under the Sixth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VI, was violated when the findings of a gunshot residue analyst who did not testify at trial and was not subject to cross-examination were admitted. The supreme court noted that the State failed to address defendant's argument that his constitutional right to confrontation was violated. This was a significant constitutional issue that compelled a response. Even after being notified of its failure to respond to the issue, the State failed to supplement its response and elected to wait until oral argument to address the constitutional issue or harmless error. Such appellate practice caused prejudice to defendant's ability to adequately prepare for or respond during oral argument. The supreme court invoked its authority under Nev. R. App. P. 31(d) and considered the State's silence to be a confession of error on the issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the district court for a new trial.

 

432 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Marvin v. Fitch


No. 52447


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


232 P.3d 425; 2010 Nev. LEXIS 18; 126 Nev. Adv. Rep. 18



May 27, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from a district court order of dismissal, certified as final under NRCP 54(b), in a 42 U.S.C. § 1983 action. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; James Todd Russell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District Court, Carson City, Nevada, granted respondents', individual members of the State Board of Equalization (State Board), motion to dismiss the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim against them by appellant taxpayers under Nev. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(5), finding that they were entitled to absolute immunity. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers challenged whether the individual members of the State Board were entitled to absolute immunity. The supreme court determined that the equalization process required the members to perform functions (fact-finding and making legal conclusions) similar to judicial officers, the process was adversarial, it applied procedural safeguards similar to a court, errors could be corrected on appeal, and the statutory scheme retained State Board members' independence from political influences. Because State Board members received evidence, rendered decisions, and regulated hearings, members of the State Board functioned like judicial officers. Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 361's notice requirements were sufficient procedural safeguards to ensure that the public was afforded due process. A taxpayer's ability to appeal the State Board's decisions and findings provided the appropriate remedy to correct errors and was indicative of a quasi-judicial proceeding. The Legislature intended the equalization process to be open to the public and that the individual taxpayer be given notice of and the opportunity to participate in the State Board's valuation of his or her property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Fodor v. State


No. 52869


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


2010 Nev. LEXIS 101



March 11, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Fodor v. State, 126 Nev. 711, 367 P.3d 769, 2010 Nev. LEXIS 733 (2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Fodor v. State, 2012 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 467 (2012)
Related proceeding at Fodor v. State, 2013 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 912 (2013)
Related proceeding at Fodor v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court of State, 2013 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 1352 (2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Fodor v. State, 2016 Nev. App. Unpub. LEXIS 548 (Nev. Ct. App., Dec. 28, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An amended information did not violate defendant's rights because the district court merely informed the State that it could amend the possession of stolen property count, the State subsequently filed a timely amended information, and the State did not charge an additional or different offense; [2]-A rational juror could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was in possession of stolen property and burglary tools because a search of the van he was using revealed copper wire consistent with the type stolen from several street lights earlier that day; [3]-Defendant failed to show that his due process rights were violated by the release of wire to the city; the record did not indicate that the State acted in bad faith by releasing the wire, that the wire had exculpatory value at the time it was released, or that the State failed to disclose the wire's existence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

437 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Mendoza-Lobos v. State


No. 52110


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 634; 218 P.3d 501; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 54; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 49



October 29, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 10, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count each of burglary, robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, sexual assault with the use of a deadly weapon, attempted sexual assault with the use of a deadly weapon, assault with a deadly weapon, and battery with a deadly weapon. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Steven P. Elliott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, pursuant to a jury verdict before the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County, Nevada, of burglary, robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, sexual assault with the use of a deadly weapon, attempted sexual assault with the use of a deadly weapon, assault with a deadly weapon, and battery with a deadly weapon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court sentenced defendant to serve consecutive sentences for a total of 35 years to life. On appeal, the supreme court considered whether certain amendments to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.165(1) violated the separation-of-powers doctrine. The supreme court also considered whether Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.165(1) required the district court to make findings on the record before imposing a sentence enhancement for the use of a deadly weapon. As to the issue of legislative authority, the mandate in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.165(1) to consider the enumerated factors when determining an appropriate sentence for a deadly weapon enhancement did not run afoul of the separation-of-powers doctrine. The supreme court agreed that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.165(1) required the district court to make findings prior to imposing a sentence for a deadly weapon enhancement. Further, the plain language of the statute required the district court to make separate findings for each deadly weapon enhancement. The supreme court concluded that nothing in the record indicated that the district court's failure to make certain findings on the record had any bearing on the district court's sentencing decision.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment of the conviction.

 

438 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Flamingo Paradise Gaming, LLC v. Chanos


No. 49223


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 502; 217 P.3d 546; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 60; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 39



September 24, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication, November 23, 2009


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal and cross-appeal from a district court judgment concerning the constitutionality of the Nevada Clean Indoor Air Act, a ballot measure passed in 2006. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Douglas W. Herndon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant establishments challenged Nevada's Clean Indoor Air Act (NCIAA), Nev. Rev. Stat. § 202.2483. The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, found portions of the statute to be unconstitutional. Respondent government officials and the establishments cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The stated purpose of the NCIAA was to protect families and children from the harmful effects of second hand smoke. On appeal, the supreme court considered whether the NCIAA was unconstitutionally vague for criminal enforcement. Concluding that it was, the supreme court next determined whether the district court properly severed the criminal provision from the statute. The supreme court considered the severance to be proper. The portion severed was not the central component of the statute and the remainder of the statute could stand alone. Nevertheless, the NCIAA passed a facial challenge for civil enforcement because this portion of the statute was not vague. The supreme court further concluded that the NCIAA did not constitute a governmental taking of private property. Business owners could still maintain possession and control over their property. The fact that they were subject to certain regulations did not result in the government taking complete control over their airspace or building property. In addition, the supreme court concluded that the NCIAA did not violate equal protection, as there were rational bases for the classifications made within the statute.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's judgment.


 

439 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Zamora v. Price


No. 51321


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 388; 213 P.3d 490; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 39; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 32



August 6, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 6, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Zamora v. Tyshae, 2009 Nev. LEXIS 48 (Nev. Sept. 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court judgment entered on a jury verdict in a tort action conducted under the short trial program. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; David B. Barker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) entered on a short trial jury's verdict in favor of respondent claimant in a new trial at the conclusion of mandatory nonbinding arbitration proceedings on tort claims arising out of an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: The case was referred to Nevada's nonbinding arbitration program pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 38.250(1). The arbitrator awarded a sum to the claimant. After a new trial, which was conducted as part of the short trial program, the jury awarded the same amount as the arbitration award. The court held that the requirement in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 38.259(2) that the arbitration award be admitted at a new trial did not deny the right to a jury trial under Nev. Const. art. 1, § 3. The mandatory jury instruction set forth in § 38.259(2)(b), which informed the jury that it was free to disregard the arbitration award and cautioned against giving the award undue weight, sufficiently addressed concerns regarding unconstitutional infringement on the jury's fact-finding role and ensured that a litigant's constitutional right to a jury trial was protected. Moreover, although there was a difference between the treatment of litigants with claims not exceeding the threshold amount in § 38.250 and litigants with larger claims, this distinction was a rational legislative choice and did not violate the equal protection guarantees set forth in U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Nev. Const. art. 4, § 21.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered on the short trial jury's verdict.

Grosjean v. Imperial Palace, Inc.


No. 44542


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 349; 212 P.3d 1068; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 33; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 30



July 30, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Grosjean v. Imperial Palace, 2009 Nev. LEXIS 70 (Nev., Oct. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal and cross-appeal from a district court judgment on a jury verdict, certified as final under NRCP 54(b), in a bifurcated civil rights/tort action. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Lee A. Gates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this action alleging a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and state law, appellant/cross-respondent detainee and respondents/cross appellants, casino and security supervisor, appealed from a judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, which denied the casino's motion to dismiss as to the punitive damages request, denied the casino's motion for judgment as a matter of law, and dismissed the detainee's state law claims.


OVERVIEW: This matter arose from an incident at the casino when casino security personnel and two Gaming Control Board (GCB) agents detained the detainee because he matched the description of a person in whom another GCB agent was interested. The relevant allegations in the complaint asserted that the detention was executed without reasonable suspicion. The instant court found that the district court properly refused to dismiss the § 1983 claims on qualified immunity grounds. The instant court reasoned that the qualified immunity doctrine did not extend to protect private actors. Next, the instant court found that the evidentiary rulings in question were within the district court's considerable discretion and that the attorney misconduct in this case, while prevalent, did not override the jury's verdict, which was based on substantial evidence in the damages phase of the trial. Finally, the instant court found that the jury's $ 500,000 award was a result of continued attorney misconduct, including a "golden rule" violation and improper emotional arguments, such that a new trial was warranted as to punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the compensatory damages portion of the district court's judgment, reversed the punitive damages portion, and remanded for a new trial on punitive damages only.

Berry v. State


No. 49709


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 265; 212 P.3d 1085; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 34; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 26



July 30, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, upon a jury verdict, of burglary while in possession of a deadly weapon, robbery with use of a deadly weapon, and one count of open and gross lewdness. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Valerie Adair, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) of burglary while in possession of a deadly weapon, robbery with use of a deadly weapon, and one count of open and gross lewdness. The appellate court addressed three issues that defendant raised on appeal and their accompanying subissues.


OVERVIEW: The district court did not err in its use of Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 202.265(5)(b), and 202.253(2) in the jury instruction. Since §§ 202.265(5)(b) and 202.253(2) defined firearm, and both definitions were included within Nev. Rev. Stat. § 193.165(6)'s definitions of deadly weapon, for enhancement purposes, a firearm under § 202.265(5)(b) was a deadly weapon. The district court did not err by instructing the jury that a firearm under §§ 202.265(5)(b) and 202.253(2) was a deadly weapon regardless of whether it was unloaded or inoperable. However, the State failed to establish either that the a toy pellet gun could fire a projectile by the force of an explosion or combustion or that it was capable of firing a metal projectile. Defendant argued unsuccessfully that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 201.210 was unconstitutionally vague. The term open was not vague, as used in § 201.210, gross sufficiently informed people what degree of lewdness was prohibited, and the terms lewd or lewdness had generally accepted meanings. The district court's jury instruction concerning his open and gross lewdness charges was adequate under plain error review.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion. The aggravated sentence for burglary while in possession of a deadly weapon and the deadly weapon enhancement sentence for the robbery conviction were reversed. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Comm'n on Ethics v. Hardy


No. 53064


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 285; 212 P.3d 1098; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 32; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 27



July 30, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order granting judicial review of a Nevada Ethics Commission decision and entering a permanent injunction in an ethics matter. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; William A. Maddox, Judge.
Comm'n on Ethics v. Hardy, 2009 Nev. LEXIS 93 (Nev., May 21, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Nevada Ethics Commission, instituted administrative proceedings against respondent state senator, asserting an ethical violation. The senator moved to dismiss the administrative proceeding on separation of powers grounds. When the motion was denied, the senator filed a petition for judicial review in the district court (Nevada), which held that the Commission was barred from proceeding against the senator. The Commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commission alleged that the senator violated Nev. Rev. Stat. § 281A.420 by failing to disclose an alleged conflict of interest regarding a senate bill and by failing to abstain from the voting on that bill. In his private capacity, the senator was president of the Associated Builders and Contractors of Southern Nevada, and the bill related to lease-purchase and installment-purchase agreements that would have affected his group's members. The court held that the Legislature's power to discipline its membership with respect to the core legislative function of voting and, by extension, disclosure of conflicts of interest, was a function constitutionally committed to each house of the Legislature under Nev. Const. art. 4, § 6, and it could not be delegated to another branch of government. Because the Commission was charged with executing the laws, Nev. Const. art. 5, § 7, it was part of the executive branch, and therefore the delegation to the Commission by the Legislature of the power to discipline its members with respect to such core legislative functions was an unconstitutional delegation of power in violation of the separation of powers provision, Nev. Const. art. 3, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.

Chavez v. State


No. 48847


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 328; 213 P.3d 476; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 35; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 29



July 30, 2009, Filed

Petition denied by Chavez v. State, 2010 Nev. LEXIS 1306 (Nev., May 10, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Chavez v. State, 2013 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 47 (2013)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of four counts of sexual assault on a child. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Robert H. Perry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), of four counts of sexual assault on his child. The district court sentenced him to four consecutive terms of life with the possibility of parole beginning after a minimum of 20 years had been served. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the child's mother were divorced but still lived together with their four children. The victim was the eldest. She told investigators that she had been molested continually for about five years, beginning at age five, when she had to have stitches in her vagina because it was torn. At the time of the preliminary hearing, discovery was almost complete. Prior to trial, the victim died. The State sought to introduce her testimony from the preliminary hearing at trial. Defendant objected that it violated his right to confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court held that the victim's testimony at the preliminary hearing was testimonial, and she was an unavailable witness. Therefore, her testimony was admissible if defendant had an opportunity for an effective cross-examination, including sufficient discovery. The court concluded that he did.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment of conviction.
