McConnell v. State


No. 49722


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 243; 212 P.3d 307; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 31; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 24



July 23, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 24, 2009, As Corrected.
Rehearing denied by McConnell v. State, 2009 Nev. LEXIS 50 (Nev., Oct. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from an order of the district court dismissing appellant's post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus in a death penalty case. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Steven R. Kosach, Judge.
McConnell v. State, 120 Nev. 1043, 102 P.3d 606, 2004 Nev. LEXIS 138 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state inmate pled guilty to, inter alia, first degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon, and the jury returned a death sentence for that charge. He appealed the decision by the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) to deny his petition without conducting an evidentiary hearing on his claims.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue was whether the constitutionality of Nevada's lethal injection protocol may be challenged in a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate argued that Nevada's lethal injection protocol violated the Eighth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution because it did not sufficiently safeguard against a substantial risk of serious harm. The constitutionality of the lethal injection protocol clearly did not involve a challenge to the validity of the conviction. Since his challenge to the lethal injection protocol would not preclude his execution under current law using another protocol, his challenge to the lethal injection protocol did not implicate the validity of the death sentence and therefore fell outside the scope of a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The district court did not err in rejecting the inmate's claim without conducting an evidentiary hearing. The district court did not err by dismissing the inmate's claims that his guilty plea was not entered knowingly and voluntarily. The district court did not err in dismissing his claims that trial and appellate counsel provided ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

Sang Man Shin v. State (In re Sang Man Shin)


No. 47995


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 100; 206 P.3d 91; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 9; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 10



March 26, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: March 26, 2009, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order setting aside as void an order sealing a criminal record. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Michelle Leavitt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a convicted sex offender, challenged a judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) setting aside as void an order sealing his criminal record, under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 179.245, upon a motion of respondent State of Nevada, Department of Public Safety (DPS).


OVERVIEW: The offender, who had pleaded guilty to attempted lewdness with a minor, successfully served a sentence of probation. After maintaining a clean criminal record for approximately 15 years, the offender received a pardon from the State Board of Pardons Commissioners. His criminal record was sealed, pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 179.245. DPS argued that the record had been erroneously sealed because, as a convicted sex offender, sealing the record was expressly precluded by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 179.245(5). The district court set aside the prior order that sealed a criminal record. The offender contended that his pardon not only cleared the civil rights restrictions attendant with his conviction, but further included the right to seal his criminal records. The court addressed the scope of the pardoning power, under Nev. Const. art. 5, § 14. The court held that the pardoning power did not bequeath innocence or erase the historical fact of the underlying criminal act and conviction. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 179.245(5) did not improperly impinge on the Pardons Board's power, and the district court did not abuse its discretion when it unsealed the criminal record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

Collins v. State


No. 50104


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 60; 203 P.3d 90; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 7; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 7



March 5, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of one count each of robbery, intimidating a public officer, and battery with substantial bodily harm. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Valerie Adair, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) convicting him of robbery, intimidating a public officer, and battery with substantial bodily harm. Defendant was adjudicated a habitual criminal and was sentenced to two concurrent prison terms of 240 months with parole eligibility after 96 months to run concurrent with a 12-month jail term.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck the victim in the face, knocking him unconscious. While the victim was unconscious, defendant rifled through the victim's pockets and took his cellular phone. When he was apprehended, defendant became extremely irate and threatened multiple public officers with physical violence. For several weeks, the victim experienced dizziness and could not bend over without almost losing consciousness. He had headaches for a month and a half. Defendant contended that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 0.060(2)'s definition of substantial bodily harm as prolonged physical pain was unconstitutionally vague. The court concluded that the phrase "prolonged physical pain," under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 0.060(2), had a well-settled and ordinarily understood meaning and, as a result, was not unconstitutionally vague. The phrase "prolonged physical pain" necessarily encompassed some physical suffering or injury that lasted longer than the pain immediately resulting from the wrongful act. The phrase was not so lacking in specific standards as to allow arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

Stromberg v. Second Judicial Dist. Court


No. 50079


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


125 Nev. 1; 200 P.3d 509; 2009 Nev. LEXIS 1; 125 Nev. Adv. Rep. 1



January 29, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Original petition for a writ of mandamus challenging a district court's decision to deny petitioner's request to apply for treatment pursuant to NRS 484.37941.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Second Judicial District Court of the State of Nevada, in and for the County of Washoe, denied defendant's application to participate in a three-year treatment program pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.37941, finding that the statute did not clearly indicate legislative intent to apply the statute retroactively. The district court granted a stay, and defendant petitioned for a writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the plain language of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.37941 applied to offenders who entered guilty pleas on or after July 1, 2007, the statute's effective date. The State argued that § 484.37941 violated the separation-of-powers doctrine by giving the district court the power to determine how to charge a DUI offender, a decision that was exclusively within the province of the executive branch of government represented by the prosecutor. The supreme court found that after the charging decision was made, any exercise of discretion permitted by the statute was simply a choice between the legislatively prescribed penalties set forth in the statute. The district court's decision to allow an offender to enter a program of treatment was analogous to the decision to sentence an offender to probation and therefore was a decision that properly fell within the discretion of the judiciary. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.37941 did not limit the prosecutor's unfettered discretion to determine whether to charge an offender for a third-time DUI or for a lesser offense.


OUTCOME: The petition for mandamus was granted and the district court had to consider defendant's request to plead guilty and apply for treatment pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.37941.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

In re Lerner


No. 49331


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 1232; 197 P.3d 1067; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 117; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 100



December 24, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Automatic review of a Southern Nevada Disciplinary Board hearing panel's recommendation that attorney Glen Lerner receive a public reprimand for violating Nevada Rule of Professional Conduct 5.5, which prohibits a lawyer from assisting in the unauthorized practice of law.



DISPOSITION: Public reprimand issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In disciplinary proceedings, respondent attorney appealed a Southern Nevada Disciplinary Board hearing panel's finding that he violated Nev. Sup. Ct. R. Prof. Conduct 5.5, which prohibits lawyers from assisting in the unauthorized practice of law, and its recommendation that he receive a public reprimand, arguing that the conduct of his law clerk did not constitute the practice of law.


OVERVIEW: A law clerk in the attorney's office was admitted to practice law in Arizona but was not admitted to practice law in Nevada. Despite this, the law clerk worked in the attorney's Las Vegas office and represented personal injury plaintiffs, attempting to negotiate settlements before filing suit. When an insurance company adjuster inquired into the law clerk's status, he learned that the law clerk was not admitted to practice law in Nevada and filed a grievance. The law clerk was found to have engaged in the unauthorized practice of law, and the attorney was found to have assisted him in such practice. On review, the court concluded that the law clerk's conduct constituted the practice of law. The law clerk routinely conducted initial client consultations and decided whether representation should be accepted, negotiated clients' claims, made legal arguments in support of a client's position, and served as the clients' sole contact in the firm. All of these activities constituted the practice of law. Because the law clerk's conduct conformed with the policies of the attorney's firm, the attorney assisted in the unauthorized practice of law.


OUTCOME: The court held that the attorney assisted another in the unauthorized practice of law in violation of Nev. Sup. Ct. R. Prof. Conduct 5.5 and ruled that a public reprimand was the proper sanction.

William M. v. State (In re William M.)


No. 48649, No. 48650


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 1150; 196 P.3d 456; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 110; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 95



November 26, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Consolidated appeals from juvenile court orders certifying appellants for criminal proceedings as adults on charges involving the use of firearms. Eighth Judicial District Court, Family Court Division, Clark County; William O. Voy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, appellant juveniles challenged orders of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Family Court Division, Clark County (Nevada) certifying the juveniles for criminal proceedings as adults, under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62B.390(2), (3).


OVERVIEW: The juveniles were over the age of 13 when they were charged, in separate cases, with offenses involving the use of a firearm. The presumptive certification statute, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62B.390(2), (3), created a rebuttable presumption that juveniles over 13 years of age and charged with certain enumerated offenses fell outside of the jurisdiction of the juvenile court and had to be transferred to the district court for adult criminal proceedings, unless there was clear and convincing evidence that the juvenile's criminal actions were substantially influenced by substance abuse or behavioral problems that might be appropriately treated within the juvenile court system, under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62B.390(3)(b). The court held that, by requiring the juveniles to admit to the charged criminal conduct in order to overcome the presumption of adult certification, under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62B.390(2), (3), the juveniles' right against self-incrimination, under U.S. Const. amend. V, was violated. Accordingly, the court declared that the entirety of Nevada's presumptive certification provisions, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 62B.390(2), (3), were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's orders certifying the juveniles as adults and remanded for further proceedings.

 

451 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. State


No. 44812


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 978; 194 P.3d 1235; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 100; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 83



October 30, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order denying a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Sally L. Loehrer, Judge.
Hernandez v. State, 118 Nev. 513, 50 P.3d 1100, 2002 Nev. LEXIS 69 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) denying a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus, relating to the imposition of the death penalty for defendant's convictions for first-degree murder, burglary while in possession of a weapon, second-degree kidnapping, and unlawful sexual penetration of a dead body.


OVERVIEW: The victim was defendant's ex-wife, and their three-year old daughter witnessed her mother's torture and killing. Defendant was sentenced to death, upon the jury's finding of three aggravating circumstances: defendant subjected the victim to nonconsensual sexual penetration, the murder was committed during a burglary, and the murder involved torture or mutilation. Appealing the denial of habeas corpus, defendant argued that the district court erred in using torture and burglary as aggravating circumstances to support the death sentence. The court agreed that the burglary aggravating circumstance should be stricken. Regarding the torture aggravating circumstance, the court held that the same conduct of torture could support a murder theory and an aggravated circumstance because Nevada's definition of torture murder sufficiently narrowed the class of persons eligible for the death penalty. Reweighing the aggravating and mitigating evidence, the court held that, absent the erroneous burglary aggravator, the jury still would have imposed death. Defendant's other post-conviction claims of ineffective assistance, including failure to challenge his competency, were all properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

452 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Cortinas v. State


No. 47905


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 1013; 195 P.3d 315; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 105; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 86



October 30, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 12, 2009.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Benavides Cortinas v. Nevada, 558 U.S. 956, 130 S. Ct. 416, 175 L. Ed. 2d 285, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7413 (2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Cortinas v. State, 2014 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 552 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, upon a jury verdict, of first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and robbery with the use of a deadly weapon. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Jennifer Togliatti, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant of first-degree murder with the use of a deadly weapon and robbery with the use of a deadly weapon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended a recent case, Nay v. State, 167 P.3d 430 (2007), required that his convictions be overturned. The supreme court disagreed, retreated from the absolute certainty approach advanced in Bolden v. State, 121 Nev. 908 (2005), and reaffirmed the harmless-error approach taken in Nay; harmless-error review applied when a general verdict could rest on a legally valid or a legally invalid alternative theory of liability. Here, although defendant was entitled to an instruction precluding the use of afterthought robbery as the predicate felony for felony murder, this instructional error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt as defendant twice confessed to the killing, led authorities to the victim's body, admitted he strangled the victim for over an hour before breaking her neck, and stabbed her in the back three times for the admitted purpose of flooding her lungs with blood. Based on this evidence alone, a rational jury would have found that the murder was willful, deliberate, and premeditated. Further, the district court correctly instructed the jury that the taking of the victim's property could occur as an afterthought to the use of force.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Harte


No. 50161


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 969; 194 P.3d 1263; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 99; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 82



October 30, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Nevada v. Harte, 556 U.S. 1257, 129 S. Ct. 2431, 174 L. Ed. 2d 227, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3911 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order partially granting a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus in a death penalty case. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Connie J. Steinheimer, Judge.
Harte v. State, 116 Nev. 1054, 13 P.3d 420, 2000 Nev. LEXIS 124 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County, Nevada, partially granting a post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus in a death penalty case.


OVERVIEW: Respondent and two codefendants murdered a cab driver during the course of a robbery. During the penalty phase of the trial, the jury found only one aggravating circumstance: the murder was committed during the course of a robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death. He filed a second post-conviction petition for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that pursuant to McConnell, the aggravating circumstance found by the jury was invalid because it was improperly based on the felony used to obtain the first-degree murder conviction. The district court concluded that the appropriate remedy for a McConnell error was a new penalty hearing, not a new trial. The Supreme Court of Nevada upheld the decision and rejected the State's contention that McConnell was wrongly decided. The State's exercise of discretion to charge respondent on alternative theories of murder did not constitute a trial error. The State's decision to base an aggravating circumstance on the robbery that was also the basis for the felony-murder theory resulted in a sentencing error.


OUTCOME: The district court's findings of fact, conclusions of law, and judgment were affirmed.

Vill. League to Save Incline Assets, Inc. v. State ex rel. Bd. of Equalization


No. 49358


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 1079; 194 P.3d 1254; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 97; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 90



October 30, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by Otto v. District Court, 126 Nev. 744, 367 P.3d 806, 2010 Nev. LEXIS 208 (Apr. 9, 2010)
Related proceeding at Berrum v. Otto, 127 Nev. 372, 255 P.3d 1269, 2011 Nev. LEXIS 37 (July 7, 2011)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Vill. League to Save Incline Assets, Inc. v. State ex rel. State Bd. of Equalization, 2012 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 279 (Feb. 24, 2012)
Decision reached on appeal by Washoe County v. Otto, 128 Nev. 424, 282 P.3d 719, 2012 Nev. LEXIS 82 (Aug. 9, 2012)
Related proceeding at Vill. League to Save Incline Assets, Inc. v. Second Judicial Dist. Court of State, 2017 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 722 (Aug. 25, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Original petition for a writ of certiorari or mandamus challenging the Nevada State Board of Equalization's review and remand of the Washoe County Board of Equalization's determination to equalize certain taxable valuations.
State ex rel. State Bd. of Equalization v. Barta, 124 Nev. 612, 188 P.3d 1092, 2008 Nev. LEXIS 63 (July 25, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Petition granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The real party in interest assessor administratively appealed a decision to respondent State Board of Equalization. The case was remanded to the County Board of Equalization. Petitioner taxpayers sought a writ of certiorari or mandamus declaring the State Board's action in remanding the matter to the County Board to be in excess of its jurisdiction or an arbitrary exercise of its discretion.


OVERVIEW: The Washoe County Board of Equalization issued a general equalization decision for a certain tax year, rolling back the taxable valuations of approximately 8,700 properties. The supreme court decided to consider the request for extraordinary relief because the taxpayers would not have the opportunity to appeal, or petition the court for judicial review of the State Board's decision to remand. The petition required the supreme court to consider whether the State Board had jurisdiction to hear the appeal from the County Board's general equalization decision. The supreme court determined that the State Board retained jurisdiction to hear the appeal, even though the statutory deadline had expired because that deadline was directory, meaning that it was advisory rather than compulsory. The State Board had discretion to remand the matter to the County Board only when the record was inadequate. The minutes in this case were sufficient to enable the State Board's review, and the State Board arbitrarily remanded the matter. Writ relief was substantively warranted.


OUTCOME: The taxpayers' request for a writ of certiorari was denied. The supreme court granted the taxpayers' petition with respect to their alternative request for a writ of mandamus.


 

455 of 673 DOCUMENTS


Knipes v. State


No. 49663


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 927; 192 P.3d 1178; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 89; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 79



October 2, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of driving under the influence causing death. Seventh Judicial District Court, Lincoln County; Steve L. Dobrescu, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence causing death. The Seventh Judicial District Court, Lincoln County, Nevada, sentenced him to serve a minimum prison term of 48 months. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a fatal accident, defendant's blood draw revealed traces of marijuana metabolite and a 0.14 blood alcohol concentration (BAC). At his trial for driving under the influence causing death, the district court permitted jurors to ask witnesses a number of questions but routinely resolved objections to those questions in unrecorded bench conferences held within the jury's presence. On an isolated occasion, the district court also asked four juror questions without first conducting one of these unrecorded hearings. The Supreme Court of Nevada held that the district court abused its discretion in failing to give the parties an opportunity to object at a bench conference; however, the procedural error was harmless, since none of the questions elicited testimony that prejudicially impacted the jury's verdict. Because a rational jury could have concluded that defendant was operating his vehicle under the influence with a BAC almost twice the legal limit when the rollover accident occurred, the evidence of his guilt was overwhelming.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ransdell v. Clark County


No. 48592


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 847; 192 P.3d 756; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 84; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 73



September 25, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court judgment in a civil action alleging various torts and constitutional violations following property abatement by Clark County. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Valorie Vega, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowner filed suit against defendant county in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), claiming that his constitutional rights had been violated and alleging trespass to land and chattels, conversion, nuisance, and negligence, all arising out of a nuisance abatement by the county. The county's motions for summary judgment were granted, and the homeowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county had received complaints that the homeowner's property was cluttered with trailers, vehicles, a bus, junk, trash, debris, and a green pool. After several notices and extensions, county personnel abated the nuisance by removing the offending vehicles and debris. The court found that the county was immune from liability under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 41.032(2), applying the Berkovitz-Gaubert two-part test. First, the actions of the county inspectors were discretionary because the abatement procedure required the inspectors to use their own judgment in assessing the conditions on the property to determine if abatement was required. The inspectors had to determine the nature of various items on the property, whether he was operating a salvage yard, and if the debris amounted to a dangerous condition in violation of the county code. Second, the county was motivated by environmental, health, and economic policies supported by the code and statutory authority. The homeowner's remaining constitutional claims, based on his assertion that the term "inoperative automobiles" was vague, failed to state a claim because property owners were not a protected class, among other reasons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

We the People Nev. v. Miller


No. 51735


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 874; 192 P.3d 1166; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 85; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 75



September 25, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Pest Comm. v. Miller, 648 F. Supp. 2d 1202, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 79466 (D. Nev., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Original petition for a writ of mandamus or prohibition challenging the constitutionality of NRS 295.056(3), which requires that an initiative petition proposing to amend the Nevada Constitution be submitted "not later than the third Tuesday in May of an even-numbered year."
People v. Sec'y of State, 238 P.3d 865, 2008 Nev. LEXIS 819 (Nev., July 16, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner political action committee (PAC) filed an original petition for a writ of mandamus or prohibition challenging the constitutionality of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 295.056(3), which required that an initiative petition proposing to amend the Nevada Constitution be submitted not later than the third Tuesday in May of an even-numbered year.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that Nev. Rev. Stat. § 295.056(3) impermissibly restricted the powers reserved to the people under Article 19 of the Nevada Constitution by establishing a submission deadline earlier than what was otherwise permitted by Nev. Const. art. XIX, §§ 2(4) and 3(2), and thereby directly inhibiting the initiative process. Therefore, § 295.056(3) was unconstitutional. The court's extraordinary intervention in this matter was warranted. The PAC had a constitutional right, under art. XIX, §§ 2(4) and 3(2), to circulate its property tax reform initiative for signatures until June 17, 2008, because the statutory submission deadline of May 20, 2008, was unconstitutional. The PAC's reasonable attempt to comply with the earlier submission deadline, later determined invalid, could not be used to defeat its constitutional right to petition, especially when the invalidity of the statutory submission deadline was unclear. Because § 295.056(3) impermissibly established a submission deadline earlier than what was otherwise permitted, i.e., May 20, 2008, that provision was unconstitutional, and the June 17, 2008, deadline under that provision's former version remained in effect.


OUTCOME: The PAC's petition for a writ of mandamus was granted.

Picetti v. State


No. 50342


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 782; 192 P.3d 704; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 76; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 68



September 11, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a guilty plea, of one count of driving under the influence (DUI), third offense within 7 years, a class B felony. Third Judicial District Court, Lyon County; Robert E. Estes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Third Judicial District Court, Lyon County (Nevada), convicting him, pursuant to a guilty plea, of one count of driving under the influence (DUI), third offense within seven years, a class B felony.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the justice courts' mass advisements and individual colloquies of defendant concerning his guilty pleas for first-offense and second-offense DUI convictions were constitutionally sufficient because he was present for the mass advisements and the justice court properly informed defendant of his right to counsel and the possible punishments he could incur as a result of entering a guilty plea. The court further held that the district court did not err by refusing to allow defendant to apply for treatment pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.37941 because the court determined that § 484.37941 did not apply retroactively, as the legislature did not clearly evince its intent for § 484.37941 to do so, and because defendant entered his guilty plea on April 30, 2007, prior to the statute's July 1, 2007 effective date. Because § 484.37941's provisions merely gave the district court discretion to allow a defendant to complete a treatment program in order to obtain a conviction and sentence for a lesser offense, the provisions were not of constitutional dimension and were not applicable retroactively.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Fergusen v. State


No. 48420


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 795; 192 P.3d 712; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 74; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 69



September 11, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Fergusen v. State, 2015 Nev. App. Unpub. LEXIS 168 (Nev. Ct. App., Apr. 15, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, upon jury verdict, of one count each of burglary, sexual assault, robbery, and first-degree kidnapping. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Stewart L. Bell, Judge.
Fergusen v. Dist. Ct., 122 Nev. 1672, 178 P.3d 753, 2006 Nev. LEXIS 815 (July 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, which convicted him of burglary, sexual assault, robbery, and first-degree kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sent to a mental health facility for a competency determination. He was eventually found competent to stand trial, and he appealed after his conviction. In reversing, the supreme court held that the Eighth Judicial District Court in Nevada had the discretion to assign the determination of all competency matters to a department under Rules of Practice for the Eighth Judicial District Court 1.30(b)(5), 1.60(a), and 3.10(b). The determination of a defendant's ongoing competency during trial had to vest with the trial judge who had been assigned to hear the matter. Defendant's request for a continuance should have been granted after his return from the facility; defendant did not have the opportunity to confer with assigned counsel, and his assigned counsel was not at the hearing. Further, defendant's fair trial rights were violated when a competency hearing was not granted. While the request for a hearing under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 178.460 might have been untimely, a hearing was warranted because defense counsel had raised reasonable doubt as to defendant not having the sufficient present ability to consult with counsel at that time.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial if defendant was competent.

Las Vegas Convention & Visitors Auth. v. Miller


No. 51509, No. 51564, No. 51639, No. 52045


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 669; 191 P.3d 1138; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 72; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 62



September 4, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Consolidated appeals and cross-appeals from final judgments concerning whether three initiative petitions qualify for placement on the ballot. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; William A. Maddox and James T. Russell, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Actions were filed in the First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada), arising out of initiatives sought to be added to the ballot by appellant proponents which would affect respondent, a convention and visitors authority. The Secretary of State determined that the circulators' affidavits for the initiatives were defective. The proponents sought relief in the district court, which upheld the Secretary of State. The proponents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The proponents' initiatives would have redirected financing received by the convention and visitors authority to other state agencies. While the parties' original actions were on appeal, the Secretary of State made the determination that the circulators' affidavits completely failed to include two statements mandated by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 295.0575: first, they did not state the number of signatures on the document, and second, they did not state that each signer had an opportunity to read the full text of the initiative before signing. The court held that substantial compliance was all that was required, but that the affidavits did not substantially comply with the statute. The proponents' efforts in the district court to cure the affidavits' defects were insufficient because the proponents failed to make a valid offer of proof necessary to show whether the circulators nevertheless complied with the statute's purposes. The court rejected the proponents' First Amendment free political speech challenge to enforcement of the affidavit requirements based on approval of similar requirements in a prior U.S. Supreme Court case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision to disqualify all three initiatives. The court affirmed in part the district court's decision in the original actions allowing the convention and visitors authority to participate in the court actions challenging the initiative petitions. The court dismissed the remaining portions of the appeal as mooted by its disqualification of the initiatives.

Miller v. Burk


No. 51768, No. 51798


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 579; 188 P.3d 1112; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 64; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 56



July 25, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Consolidated original petitions for extraordinary writ relief that seek to exclude real parties in interest's names from the 2008 primary and general election ballots based on the Nevada Constitution's Article 15, Section 3(2) term-limit provision.



DISPOSITION: Petitions granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After real parties in interest candidates (running for reelection to state offices and local governing bodies) filed their candidacies, petitioners, the Nevada Secretary of State and an elector, challenged the candidates' qualifications, seeking writs of mandamus directing the respective filing officers to exclude the candidates names from the upcoming primary and general election under the term-limit provision, Nev. Const. art. XV, § 3(2).


OVERVIEW: In consolidated writ proceedings, the Secretary of State and the elector challenged the qualifications of eight candidates; the candidates, who had concededly held their positions since 1997, disputed whether the term-limit amendment applied to bar them from serving another term starting in 2009. The supreme court concluded that under Nev. Const. art. XV, § 3(2), if a person had served, or at the conclusion of his or her current term would have served, 12 years or more in an office or a position on a local governing body, that person could not be reelected to that office or position. Without any demonstration that precedent concluding that a ballot question which enacted the term limit amendment met the constitutional "same manner" requirement was clearly erroneous, the supreme court could not disavow it. Thus, the supreme court held that term-limit amendment was validly enacted. As the candidates, at the conclusion of their current terms, would have served at least 12 years in their respective offices, they could not be elected to their current positions. Accordingly, mandamus relief was appropriate, and the candidates names were excluded from the upcoming general election ballot.


OUTCOME: Mandamus relief was granted and the candidates names were excluded from the upcoming general election ballot.

State ex rel. State Bd. of Equalization v. Barta


No. 47397, No. 47398, No. 47399, No. 47400, No. 47401


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 612; 188 P.3d 1092; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 63; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 58



July 25, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Vill. League to Save Incline Assets, Inc. v. State ex rel. Bd. of Equalization, 124 Nev. 1079, 194 P.3d 1254, 2008 Nev. LEXIS 97 (2008)
Related proceeding at Lowe v. Washoe County, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 30072 (D. Nev., Mar. 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Consolidated appeals from district court orders granting combined petitions for judicial review and complaints for relief, overturning a decision of the Nevada State Board of Equalization regarding parcels of Washoe County real property. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.
State ex rel. State Bd. of Equalization v. Bakst, 122 Nev. 1403, 148 P.3d 717, 2006 Nev. LEXIS 143 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent taxpayers challenged appellant county assessor's appraisal methods to establish the taxable values of properties. Appellant county and appellant State Boards of Equalization denied relief. The taxpayers petitioned for judicial review. The First Judicial District Court, Carson City, Nevada, granted the taxpayers' petitions. The appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: To arrive at the taxable value for the subject land, the assessor relied on sales prices of properties in the surrounding area, adjusting the sales prices of those properties and the land's valuation based on the properties' comparable views, beachfront qualities, times of sale, and planned uses. The State and county contended that, even if unconstitutional methods were used to determine the properties' taxable values, the district court's orders granting the petitions for judicial review should be reversed because the taxpayers failed to prove that their properties' taxable values exceeded their full cash values. That position, however, disregarded a taxpayer's right to a uniform and equal rate of assessment and taxation, which was guaranteed by Nev. Const. art. X, § 1. A property value determined using unconstitutional, nonuniform methods was necessarily unjust and inequitable. Thus, because the methods used to value a taxpayer's property were a material consideration in determining whether the property was justly and equitably valued, the taxpayers could challenge an assessment based on the use of unconstitutional methods even if the assessment did not exceed full cash value.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's decision.

Moldon v. County of Clark


No. 47549


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 507; 188 P.3d 76; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 66; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 49



July 24, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Moldon v. Clark County Dist. Court Clerk, 2011 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 1007 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order, certified as final under NRCP 54(b), denying a motion for interest in an eminent domain action. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Douglas W. Herndon, Judge.
City of Las Vegas Downtown Redevelopment Agency v. Crockett, 117 Nev. 816, 34 P.3d 553, 2001 Nev. LEXIS 71 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an eminent domain proceeding, the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, granted a redevelopment agency immediate occupancy and possession of the property. A settlement agreement was reached. Appellant condemnees requested an order directing the district court clerk to pay them principal and interest on an amount deposited with the court. Respondent county opposed the request, and the request was denied. The condemnees appealed.


OVERVIEW: As part of the settlement agreement in the underlying proceeding, the condemnees were entitled to the full amount of the condemnation deposit. On appeal, the supreme court considered whether the placement of interest earned on condemnation funds, which were deposited with the court into a local government's general fund for public benefit, pursuant to statute, constituted a taking under the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. The supreme court concluded that, because condemnation deposits constituted private property to the extent that a party was entitled to the condemnation deposit, the condemnees were likewise entitled to the interest earned on that deposit. The placement of the interest into the local government's general fund for public benefit, that act constituted a taking under the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments. Former Nev. Rev. Stat. 355.210 (pre-2007 amendment) was unconstitutionally applied to allow such takings.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the district court's order, and the matter was remanded to the district court so that the district court could determine the amount of interest owed to the condemnees on the condemnation deposit.

City of Las Vegas v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court of Nev.


No. 48469


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 540; 188 P.3d 55; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 58; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 51



July 24, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Original petition for a writ of mandamus challenging a district court order reversing a municipal court conviction of domestic battery and remanding the matter for conviction and sentencing for simple battery.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner City prosecuted real party in interest defendant for misdemeanor battery constituting domestic violence. Defendant appealed, and the district court (Nevada) ordered the judgment of conviction amended to reflect a conviction for simple battery without a domestic violence sentencing enhancement and remanded the case for resentencing. The City petitioned for mandamus relief.


OVERVIEW: In its petition for a writ of mandamus, the City requested that the district court be directed to recognize that the battery defendant committed constituted domestic battery under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 33.018 based upon defendant's relationship with the victim as his sister-in-law. The supreme court concluded that, based on the plain meaning of § 33.018, a battery by a sister-in-law on a brother-in-law fell within the definition of domestic violence. Consequently, the district court improperly amended the judgment of conviction to reflect simple battery without a domestic violence enhancement, and mandamus relief was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The City's petition for a writ of mandamus was granted.

 

465 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Halverson v. Miller


No. 51539


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 484; 186 P.3d 893; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 51; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 47



July 3, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Original petition for a writ of mandamus or prohibition, and request for declaratory relief, challenging the constitutionality of Senate Bill 195, enacted as Chapter 436 of the 2005 Statutes of Nevada, which amended NRS 3.018.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner district court judge filed an original petition for a writ of mandamus or prohibition and a request for declaratory relief, which challenged the constitutionality of Sen. Bill 195 (Nev. 2005), amending Nev. Rev. Stat. § 3.018. The judge sought to prevent respondents, Nevada Secretary of State and a county registrar of voters, from holding the next election for four judicial positions created by Bill 195.


OVERVIEW: The judge, who held one of the positions created by Bill 195, argued that Bill 195 unconstitutionally created positions for judges with initial terms of two years, when the Nevada Constitution required six-year terms for all district court judges. She sought to have her two year term changed to a six-year term. Upon review, the court determined that Bill 195 did not violate the Nevada Constitution because the Nevada Constitution provided the Nevada Legislature with the ability to create new judicial positions for less than six-year initial terms in order to place judicial positions on the same election cycle. Statutes creating judicial positions with shortened initial terms to preserve a uniform general election cycle were constitutional. In addition, a judge selected for a shortened initial term had no right to later claim entitlement to a full six-year term. Finally, although the two-year term limitation was not enacted in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 3.018 when it was amended to add judges to the Eight Judicial District, the limitation was enacted in the official Statutes of Nevada.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.

Somee v. State


No. 45604


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 434; 187 P.3d 152; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 48; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 42



July 3, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Somee v. State, 2012 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 814 (2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Somee v. State, 2014 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 427 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, pursuant to a jury verdict, of four counts of attempted murder with the use of a deadly weapon with the intent to promote, further, or assist a criminal gang and two counts of carrying a concealed weapon. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Michelle Leavitt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada) convicting him of four counts of attempted murder with the use of a deadly weapon with the intent to promote, further, or assist a criminal gang and two counts of carrying a concealed weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting the victims during a fight between rival gang members. On appeal, the court held that because the district court failed to conduct an evidentiary hearing on defendant's motion to suppress a gun and brass knuckles found on his person during a pat down search and failed to make factual findings about the circumstances surrounding the search prevented the court from reviewing its decision. On remand, the district court was instructed to conduct an evidentiary hearing and made factual findings. The district court was also directed to determine whether the evidence obtained in police officers' field interviews with defendant prior to the instant crimes should have been admitted under the standards set forth by the court. The court held that the district court did not err by admitting the field interviews as improper evidence of defendant's bad character under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 48.045 because the evidence was relevant to the gang enhancement for the charged crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were reversed and the case was remanded to the district court for an evidentiary hearing on defendant's motion to suppress evidence found on his person during the pat down search. The district court was directed to make specific factual findings and apply the legal standard as articulated in the opinion.

Diomampo v. State


No. 47224


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 414; 185 P.3d 1031; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 44; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 41

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury before the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant of mid-level trafficking in a controlled substance in violation of Nevada's Uniform Controlled Substances Act. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police officers effected a routine traffic stop on an automobile driven by defendant. Defendant was placed under arrest because of outstanding warrants. Drugs were found in a fanny pack and inside a sunglass case that was under the vehicle's floormat. On appeal, defendant contended, inter alia, that: the State used its peremptory challenges improperly, the State improperly commented on defendant's post-Miranda silence, and the State improperly introduced character evidence, which was prohibited by Nev. Rev. Stat. § 48.045(2). The supreme court concluded that the State violated Batson because, with respect to two of the jurors, the State's challenges were false and pretextual. Moreover, an officer's comments that methamphetamine users supported their habits by committing robberies affected defendant's substantial rights. The supreme court found, however, that the search of the vehicle was lawful. The supreme court also determined that evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction, but the errors required reversal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed. The matter was remanded for a new trial.

 

468 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Hamm v. Arrowcreek Homeowners' Ass'n


No. 47763


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 290; 183 P.3d 895; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 30; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 28



May 15, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order dismissing a homeowners' action that sought to release a homeowners' association lien. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Steven P. Elliott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners sued respondent homeowners' association and collection agency, seeking , inter alia, a declaration interpreting the covenants, conditions, and restrictions so as to eliminate any assessment fees on a vacant lot. The Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada), dismissed the complaint because the homeowners had not submitted the claims to mediation under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 38.319 (2007). The homeowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 38.310 (2007), a district court had to dismiss disputes arising from the interpretation, application, or enforcement of homeowners' associations' covenants, conditions, and restrictions if the parties did not first submit the dispute to mediation or arbitration. This requirement did not apply to actions for injunctive relief involving an immediate threat of irreparable harm, or actions relating to the title to residential property. On an issue of first impression, the filing of a lien, in and of itself, did not create an immediate threat of irreparable harm. An action to release a lien, without more, did not relate to the title to residential property. As neither of these exceptions was shown, the homeowners were required to submit their claims to mediation or arbitration before instituting their action. Moreover, § 38.310 applied to a collection agency that acted as the association's agent. Since the homeowners had not first submitted their claims against the homeowners' association and the collection agency to mediation or arbitration as required by § 38.310, the district court properly dismissed their complaint.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the homeowners' action was affirmed.

Johanson v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court of Nev.


No. 48028


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 245; 182 P.3d 94; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 25; 36 Media L. Rep. 2252; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 23



May 1, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Original petition for a writ of mandamus or prohibition challenging a district court order sealing the entire case and restricting all communication regarding the underlying divorce proceedings.
Johanson v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court of Nev., 173 P.3d 718, 2007 Nev. LEXIS 76 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who was a party in underlying divorce proceedings, filed an original petition for a writ of mandamus or prohibition challenging a Nevada district court's ruling that ordered the entire case file sealed and that imposed a gag order, sua sponte, restricting all parties and their attorneys from discussing the case with the public.


OVERVIEW: At the time petitioner and real party in interest were divorced, real party in interest was a district court judge, but real party in interest failed to get reelected. Subsequently, real party in interest again ran for a district court judgeship. The instant court concluded that by failing to comply with Nev. Rev. Stat. § 125.110 when it sealed the entire case file, the district court manifestly abused its discretion. Section 125.110(2) allowed the district court to seal only certain documents in a divorce proceeding and only upon a party's written request. Even if the district court retained inherent authority to seal the record in divorce cases, real party in interest failed to demonstrate that the order sealing the entire case file was a necessary exercise of that power to protect his or any other person's rights or to otherwise administer justice. The gag order was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The district court failed to consider whether potential publicity posed a serious and imminent threat to a protected competing interest. Real party in interest's judicial campaign had no apparent bearing on the administration of justice or any other protected interest.


OUTCOME: A writ of mandamus was issued directing the district court to vacate its order sealing the entire case file and the gag order restricting all communication regarding the case.

Father & Sons & Daughter v. Transp. Servs. Auth. of Nev.


No. 47156, No. 47349


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 254; 182 P.3d 100; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 26; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 24



May 1, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Consolidated appeals from district court orders denying petitions for judicial review in common carrier certification matters. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Valerie Adair (No. 47156) and Douglas W. Herndon (No. 47349), Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, affirmed the decision of respondent Transportation Services Authority of Nevada (TSA) levying fines against appellant company for alleged violations of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 706.386, which proscribed fully regulated common motor carriers from operating as carriers of intrastate commerce without first obtaining a certificate of public convenience and necessity. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company argued that it was not within Nev. Rev. Stat. § 706.386's reach because the company never held itself out to the public as willing to transport property by vehicle. The supreme court disagreed. The record supported the TSA's determination that the company's course of business illustrated its true identity as a fully regulated common motor carrier. The company held itself out to the public as a referral service for individual movers by placing telephone directory advertisements. The company referred its customers to individual loader/packers only after those customers rented a moving vehicle from another company, which was owned by the same persons. The company's scheme was designed to accomplish conduct plainly regulated by the TSA: intrastate operations carried out by public moving services. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 706.137 was not constitutionally vague as it neither forbade nor required any action, and the TSA was not authorized to regulate anyone who merely engaged in the transportation of household goods. It was narrowly tailored to protect the public from unlicensed, uninsured, and unregistered common motor carriers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

471 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Chanos v. Nev. Tax Comm'n


No. 48292


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 232; 181 P.3d 675; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 24; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 22



April 24, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at S. Cal. Edison v. First Judicial Dist. Court, 255 P.3d 231, 2011 Nev. LEXIS 25 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order dismissing a complaint to void a tax commission decision for open meeting law violations. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Nevada Attorney General filed a complaint under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 241.037, to void refunds provided respondent taxpayer, granted by respondent Nevada Tax Commission, in violation of the Open Meeting Law, Nev. Rev. Stat. § 241.020. The First Judicial District Court, Carson City, Nevada, dismissed the complaint, and the Attorney General appealed.


OVERVIEW: The case arose from the Tax Commission's decision, following a series of hearings that it closed to the public, to grant the taxpayer a refund of use taxes it paid from 1998 to 2000. Thereafter, believing that the Tax Commission violated the Open Meeting Law by deliberating and voting on the taxpayer's appeal in closed sessions, the Attorney General filed a complaint to void the refunds. The court ruled that the Tax Commission violated the Open Meeting Law to the extent that it received nonconfidential evidence, deliberated, and voted on the taxpayer's tax appeal in closed sessions. Former Nev. Rev. Stat. § 360.247 created a limited exception to the Open Meeting Law, under which the Tax Commission could close, at a taxpayer's request, only the portion of the Tax Commission's session at which it received confidential evidence, and questioned witnesses, and heard argument concerning confidential information. The exception did not permit the Tax Commission to hold all portions of the taxpayer appeal hearings in closed sessions. Under the Open Meeting Law, the Tax Commission was required to receive nonconfidential evidence, deliberate, and vote in open session.


OUTCOME: The order of dismissal was reversed.


 

472 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Andersen Family Assocs. v. Ricci


No. 47878


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 182; 179 P.3d 1201; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 19; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 17



March 27, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order denying judicial review in a water law matter. First Judicial District Court, Carson City; Michael R. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant water right owner sued respondents, a city and the State Engineer, challenging a decision that pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 533.085(1), the cancellation of the city's permit did not result in a loss of priority for the water rights that it had purchased. The First Judicial District Court, Carson City (Nevada) denied the owner's petition. The owner appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue was whether the city had lost priority in certain vested water rights after the State Engineer canceled and later reinstated a permit modifying the use of those rights pursuant to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 533.395. Two unambiguous statutes were in conflict: Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 533.085(1) and 533.395(3). The argument that vested water rights could be lost by applying for and receiving a permit modifying the use of those rights failed as nothing in Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 533 or prior case law suggested that an application to modify vested rights amounted to intentional abandonment of those rights. Thus, the cancellation and later reinstatement of the city's permit did not affect its underlying vested rights. Although it lost the right to use the water in the approved manner when the permit was cancelled, it did not lose the priority attached to its vested rights because such a result would have impaired the city's vested rights in violation of Nev. Rev. Stat. § 533.085(1). The city's decision to apply for a permit did not subject its water rights to Nev. Rev. Stat. § 533.395(3) because although it changed the use, its vested rights remained of the same character.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Sparks Nugget v. State ex rel. Dep't of Taxation


No. 45755


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


124 Nev. 159; 179 P.3d 570; 2008 Nev. LEXIS 17; 124 Nev. Adv. Rep. 15



March 27, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Nugget v. State, 2008 Nev. LEXIS 54 (Nev., July 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court summary judgment in a sales and use tax refund case. Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County; Brent T. Adams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Nevada Department of Taxation denied the appellant hotel's refund claim. The hotel appealed to the tax commission, but the appeal was unsuccessful. The hotel then brought suit, before the Second Judicial District Court, Washoe County (Nevada) against the Tax Department. The district court granted summary judgment in favor of the Tax Department. The hotel appealed.


OVERVIEW: The hotel, which was a hotel and casino resort, operated a number of restaurants. The hotel purchased a large quantity of unprepared food, upon which the hotel paid no sales or use tax. The hotel then served the food in one of two ways: as purchases through its restaurants or as complimentary meals. The hotel paid use tax on the food it used to prepare complimentary meals. In its refund claim, the hotel argued that the food it purchased and used for complimentary meals was not subject to either sales or use tax. The application of use tax was the primary issue on appeal. The supreme court agreed with the hotel because the taxes collected in this case were unconstitutional, pursuant to Nev. Const. art. 10, § 3(A). The use of its tax-exempt food to prepare and distribute complimentary patron and employee meals did not constitute a taxable event under Nevada's food exemption. The constitutionally mandated exemption applied to all "food for human consumption," unless that food was prepared food intended for immediate consumption. The hotel was entitled to a refund of the use taxes paid on the meals, and the district court erred in granting the Tax Department summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the district court's summary judgment denying the hotel's refund claim.

Grey v. State

No. 48028


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


173 P.3d 718; 2007 Nev. LEXIS 76; 123 Nev. Adv. Rep. 58



December 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion at Johanson v. Eighth Judicial Dist. Court of Nev., 124 Nev. 245, 182 P.3d 94, 2008 Nev. LEXIS 25 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Original petition for a writ of mandamus or prohibition challenging a district court order sealing the entire case and restricting all communication regarding the underlying divorce proceedings.
Johanson v. Lueck, 123 Nev. 828, 210 P.3d 740, 2007 Nev. LEXIS 657 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former wife filed a request for a writ of mandamus or prohibition challenging an order entered by respondents, a trial judge and the Eighth Judicial District Court of the State of Nevada, in and for the County of Clark, sealing an entire divorce case and restricting communication regarding the underlying divorce proceedings involving real party in interest former husband.

Wilson v. State


No. 46942


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


123 Nev. 587; 170 P.3d 975; 2007 Nev. LEXIS 69; 123 Nev. Adv. Rep. 54



November 21, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from an amended judgment of conviction entered following a remand from this court. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Michelle Leavitt, Judge.
Wilson v. State, 121 Nev. 345, 114 P.3d 285, 2005 Nev. LEXIS 35 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County (Nevada), which entered an amended judgment of conviction after a remand for resentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of using a minor in the production of pornography and four counts of possession of a visual presentation depicting sexual conduct of a person under 16 years of age. He was sentenced to 4 terms of 24 to 72 months on the possession charges to run concurrently with 4 consecutive terms of 10 years to life on the production charges. Three of the four production convictions were reversed, and the case was remanded for rensentencing. The district court increased the minimum sentence and ordered that the sentences run consecutively. This appeal followed. In vacating, the supreme court noted that the Dolby case held that the vacation of a lawful sentence on one count did not permit a district court to increase a lawful sentence imposed on a separate count. Dolby embodied the double jeopardy policy followed in Nevada, and the federal courts' approach to this issue was rejected. The supreme court extended Dolby to apply to resentencings mandated on appeal. Finally, the district court's resentencing on the lawful portions of defendant's conviction surviving direct appeal violated his rights against double jeopardy under Nev. Const. art. 1, § 8(1).


OUTCOME: The amended judgment of conviction was vacated. The case was remanded to the district court with instructions to reinstate the portions of defendant's original sentence that were affirmed on direct appeal.

Douglas Disposal, Inc. v. Wee Haul, LLC


No. 44862


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


123 Nev. 552; 170 P.3d 508; 2007 Nev. LEXIS 62; 123 Nev. Adv. Rep. 51



November 8, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a district court order denying injunctive relief to enforce an exclusive franchise agreement. Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County; David R. Gamble, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant disposal company brought an action against respondent rivals, requesting injunctive relief and damages based on the company's exclusive franchise agreement with a county for construction waste collection and disposal. The Ninth Judicial District Court, Douglas County (Nevada) denied relief, holding that the agreement unduly burdened interstate commerce in violation of the dormant Commerce Clause. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court found that non-putrescible construction debris was not injurious to the public health and therefore fell outside of the county's police power. The supreme court disagreed, noting that such construction waste could contain materials adverse to human health and posed other safety hazards. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 444.510(1) required local governments to develop a plan to provide for a solid waste management system, and Nev. Rev. Stat. §§ 244.187(3) and 244.188(1)(b) authorized counties to grant exclusive franchises for the collection and disposal of garbage and "other waste," including construction waste. The district court erred when it found that the exclusive franchise agreement violated the dormant Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, because: (1) the county had a legitimate if not compelling health and safety interest in regulating construction waste through an exclusive franchise; (2) no unequal burden on interstate commerce had been created, as the disposal company's rivals were no more affected by the agreement than any other intrastate or interstate firms; and (3) the rivals did not argue that an available, less burdensome alternative existed.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the district court's order denying the injunction and remanded the matter to the district court for further proceedings.

Nelson v. State


No. 46353


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


123 Nev. 534; 170 P.3d 517; 2007 Nev. LEXIS 63; 123 Nev. Adv. Rep. 50

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, in part, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Nelson v. McDaniel, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 19542 (D. Nev., Feb. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a judgment of conviction, upon a jury verdict, of conspiracy to commit robbery, robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, and failure to stop on the signal of a police officer. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Donald M. Mosley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, convicted defendant of conspiracy to commit robbery, robbery with the use of a deadly weapon, and failure to stop on the signal of a police officer. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the conviction for "failure to stop" under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 484.348(3)(b) was unconstitutionally unfair. The supreme court noted that the term "endangers," as used in the statute, was not unconstitutionally vague when considered in the context of the entire statute. The statute gave fair notice to people of ordinary intelligence that an individual was committing a felony when they drove in such a manner as to endanger persons or property while fleeing from a police vehicle with its lights and sirens activated. The district court did not err by failing to sua sponte excuse the veniremember for cause where she would not be biased. Defendant's proposed jury instructions were properly rejected as they were duplicative and misstated Nevada law. Defendant's habitual criminal sentence was authorized by statute.

In re Halverson


No. 49876


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


123 Nev. 493; 169 P.3d 1161; 2007 Nev. LEXIS 57; 123 Nev. Adv. Rep. 48



November 1, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Halverson v. Nev. Comm'n on Judicial Discipline (In re Halverson), 2011 Nev. Unpub. LEXIS 24 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from an order of the Nevada Commission on Judicial Discipline, which imposed an interim suspension upon a district court judge.
Halverson v. Hardcastle, 123 Nev. 245, 163 P.3d 428, 2007 Nev. LEXIS 38 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a district court judge, appealed an order of the Nevada Commission on Judicial Discipline, which imposed an interim suspension upon her.


OVERVIEW: This case pending before the supreme court raised several issues of first impression concerning a rarely used but formidable power available to the Nevada Commission on Judicial Discipline to temporarily suspend a judge before conducting a formal hearing. The Commission did not abuse its discretion in determining that the totality of the circumstances justified the interim suspension of the judge based on her: (1) inability to adequately conduct criminal trials; (2) abusive behavior toward court personnel, including sexual harassment and creating a hostile work environment; (3) falling asleep on the bench; and (4) failure to cooperate with colleagues and court administration. As the Commission's procedures accorded the judge due process, the court rejected her challenges to the suspension on this basis. Because the Commission entered its suspension order before any formal statement of charges was filed, its hearing on the suspension was closed. The denial of the judge's request to subpoena documents concerning other judicial disciplinary proceedings was not a violation of due process. Nev. Rev. Stat. § 1.467(3) was not unconstitutionally vague.

480 of 673 DOCUMENTS



Martinez v. Maruszczak


No. 44347


SUPREME COURT OF NEVADA


123 Nev. 433; 168 P.3d 720; 2007 Nev. LEXIS 54; 123 Nev. Adv. Rep. 43



October 11, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a declaratory judgment in a medical malpractice case. Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County; Mark R. Denton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, heirs and an administratrix of a decedent's estate, filed wrongful death claims for medical malpractice against defendant physician. The Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County, Nevada, converted the action to a declaratory judgment action. The district court held that the physician was not a state employee entitled to sovereign immunity. The physician appealed. Amicus curiae challenged Nev. Rev. Stat. § 41.035(1)'s damages cap.


OVERVIEW: The practice of medicine as a governmental function did not fall outside the scope of Nev. Rev. Stat. ch. 41's provisions. Because he was a paid employee of a state agency, the physician was a state employee when he treated the deceased. In deciding whether the physician's acts were discretionary, the court adopted and applied the Berkovitz-Gaubert approach articulated by the U.S. Supreme Court for determining the scope of discretionary-act immunity. As the physician did not engage in policy-making decisions in his treatment of the deceased, he was not entitled to immunity from suit under Nev. Rev. Stat. § 41.032(2). While the physician was not entitled to discretionary-function immunity, his status as a state employee entitled him to the statutory cap on tort damages set forth in Nev. Rev. Stat. § 41.035(1). The court rejected the argument that the damages cap violated constitutional equal protection and due process principles. Rational bases existed for treating public and private physicians differently, namely; the state treasury remained a legitimate state interest, and the state's interest in encouraging qualified professionals to accept state employment was legitimate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's declaratory judgment.
